Writings Index

Dreaming in Death City

part - Arrival

It had been another bad day at work. Kali had arrived late as usual, only this time the boss was watching. With a shake of his head he had escorted her to his office where he had given her an official warning about continuous lateness. At the end he had presented the papers for her to sign. Bold on the top were the words "First Warning". As she was leaving his office he added, "By the way, lose the cape. You're too old to be playing goth dress-up. It's not professional." She bit back a reply but couldn't stop the cold dagger stare as she turned to leave. Behind her he leaned back in his chair and grinned at her stiff posture.

She stalked to her desk in the basement shop and set about the meaningless tasks that filled her days. A little surfing of the internet and programming of the work flow system that no one would ever use. By the time she was ready to leave the watery sunshine had turned to a cold Seattle drizzle. She climbed slowly onto the bus, grateful for the unprofessional cloak that had kept her mostly dry.

The bus was packed full of soggy bodies by the time it reached Broadway. She had to push and thread her way to the nearest door and yell for the driver to open it again. She stepped out into the crowds and bustle of the brightly lit street. Neon flashed and pulsed, the overhead cables snapped and popped as other buses crawled along the street. Voices were raised in shouts of greeting and conversations as she tried to find space on the sidewalks to move. Carefully she eased her way through the throng to her favorite East Indian restaurant. She settled into a booth near the door, one of the few still empty, and placed her order. She had just leaned back to relax when the door opened again. She glanced up in time to see her ex-partner Anne entering with her new boyfriend.

They were laughing and carrying on like they had been together for months instead of a couple of weeks. As they walked by Anne turned to him and said in a loud whisper, "There she is. God, I can't believe I stayed with that depressed psycho chick as long as I did. And that's not the worst of it, let me tell you..." As they walked away Kali dropped enough money for her order plus a healthy tip and fled back into the night.

For once she was grateful for the rain. It gave her an excuse to pull the hood up on her cloak as she slipped into the shadows of the nearest alley. Eyes burning with unshed tears she slipped through the dark to the next street back, away from the lights and crowds of Broadway. Head bowed from more than the ever present drizzle, she shuffled along thinking of the last few days. With a heavy sigh she slipped back onto Broadway to walk past the stairway to nowhere, the last remains of a long demolished building. Just visible through the now stronger rain, it curved up to Harvard Street and then swept up to the missing building.

It tugged at her like a half remembered dream and slowed her footsteps. Her gaze was so focused on the shadowed bulk of the stairs that she almost didn't see one of the chains holding the fence together was gone. Spurred by her depressed not caring she shoved and pulled the fence sections apart enough to squeeze through. Slowly she climbed the rotting concrete steps until she stood at the top where the building should have been.

The rain dripped slowly from her cloak as she stared into the darkness as if waiting for the building to materialize in front of her. For a flickering moment she thought she saw it shimmering in the shadows, then it was gone. A faint popping sound intruded on her awareness and twitched her head toward Broadway. Nothing seemed out of place.

She turned to look at Harvard Street. A spill of warm yellow light pulled her gaze to an old trolley parked nearby. Curios, she slowly walked to the fence on Harvard and pushed her way through the gap she found there. The trolley was old, boxy, with a raised section in the center of the roof for ventilation. It was made of black painted wood, with domed glass widows, and it sat on railroad wheels instead of tires. She carefully approached the trolley looking for markings or signs. Near the door was an elegant insignia with "DCM-Eternia" blazoned on it. She was about to turn away when the doors opened and a voice called out, "A cold, wet night out, isn't it lady?"

"That it is," she replied, peering in at the driver. He was dressed in a worn long tailed coat and black top hat that would have looked more at home in a horse cab than the trolley. "What insignia is this?"

"Death City Metro, lady. Don't ye remember? Ye requested a ride on the Death City Metro. I am here to offer it to ye."

She froze as her mind shut off for long moments. "That...that was just..." She stopped and sucked in a deep breath and thought again of the endless tomorrows stretching off into boredom. For long moments she hesitated, trapped by fear of the unknown, then with a shake of her head she decided. "Wicked!"

"Oh no lady, we be not wicked. Death City be neutral in the Proxy Wars."

"Oh, um..." Kali groped around for an appropriate exclamation and finally gave up. "I'm just very glad to see you."

She moved to step aboard only to stop as he said, "That be not good enough, lady. Ye must answer yeah or nay."

The words came to her from somewhere deep in the past, from dreams and stories. "I enter freely and of my own will." The words hung in the air for a moment, ancient and powerful.

"Then enter and be welcome aboard the Death City Metro, lady..."

"Kali," she replied.

"Welcome Kali and Blessed Be." The exchange had the feel of a spell or ritual because once it was done he reverted back to the friendly trolley driver. "Take a seat anywhere ye like. The ride be a bit rough at first when we be leavin' the Realms." As he spoke he set the tram in motion. Within moments it lifted from the street and climbed into the clouds. Kali watched spell-bound as Seattle faded into the distance.

She sat back in the worn high backed leather seat and wondered what was happening. Part of her expected to wake shortly and find herself huddled on the stairs to nowhere. Another part fervently prayed this was really happening. Thoughts zipped through her head as she remembered the emails to her friend Jack about the stories he had written. In one of his latest he had asked if she had wanted to take a trip to Death City. "No, this can't be..."

It slipped out quietly but the coachman heard it anyway. "What was that, Lady Kali?"

"Ummm...nothing..."

"Sammi and Jemima asked that someone come for ye. They said a friend told them ye'd be wantin' te visit. Now settle back, we've a bit of journey left. It'll be about an hour to the Portal and then another two hours from the Portal to the city. Ye can ask after it at the Adam n' Eve. Ye be expected."

She expected to stay wide awake with thoughts bouncing around her head. Instead she felt her eyes drift closed and she faded into sleep moments later.


The driver's voice slowly called her back awake, "We have arrived Lady Kali." Outside the tram wrought iron gas lamps lit a wide street. A sweep of cobbled path swept from the street to the brooding dark doors of a large cathedral. A smaller stone path lead off to the right side. "Welcome to Death City, the capital of Eternia. They be waiting for ye at the Adam and Eve pub. Follow the path around the edge of the cathedral and ye’ll find it soon enough. Tell the landlord’s daughter yer a friend of Jemima." Still she hesitated until he said again, "Go on lady, they're expecting ye."

Carefully she climbed down into the rainy night. A steady drizzle kept her company as she slowly walked down the path. At least some things were familiar. The pub was right where the driver had said. A pool of gaslight illuminated the worn oak door and the sign hanging above. Age darkened brick work formed the bulk of the building. Warm light spilled from the windows casting pools on the outside tables and herb gardens near the entry.

She stood in the shadows for long moments staring at the building. Finally she shrugged, gathered her courage and strode to the door. She pulled it open onto a warm, cheery but tiny common room with a large fire burning at one end. Conversations washed over her as she stared in at the crowd. Tables were pushed together randomly to fill the available space. A thin, blonde server wove her way skillfully through the crowded chaos, leaving food and beer while efficiently removing the empties.

Cautiously she stepped in and let the door close. Moving carefully she tried to thread her way to the imposing bar directly in front of her and the giant holding forth from behind it. She was making headway when a tangle of flying skirts and a happy voice interrupted her progress.

"Kali! It is you, isn't it? We knew you were coming. I'm so glad to meet you! Come on, let me get you a place and something to drink. I'll put you at Sammi and Jemima's table. Follow me. It's down in the vault." Immediately the girl was winding her way through the crowd with practiced ease. Kali followed her through another common room to a spiral stairway of brick leading down to an enormous brick chamber below the inn. Thick Columns arched up to support the building above. Gas lights painted flickering shadows around the room, and a huge fireplace idled along with a fire just large enough to keep the room comfortable. Soon she had Kali planted at a small table to the side of the large hearth. "Don't worry as a friend of Sammi and Jemima it’s ok to be at their table. I'm Josephine by the way, but everyone calls me Jo. Big Joe, my da, is behind the bar. What can I get you?"

Kali, still stunned by it all, answered hesitantly, "Something dark..."

"Dark?"

"Umm dark and heavy. You know, something you could walk on and not leave tracks."

"Got it! One Murphy’s Imperial coming up." Jo skittered away in another flurry of skirts leaving Kali staring bemusedly into the room. A few minutes later she was back with a mug of beer and a small plate of bread and cheese. "Here, and I brought food in case you're hungry." She perched on the other chair before continuing, "Now, I'm sure you have questions..."

"Yeah, but the first is easy, how do I settle up for the beer?"

"Don't worry about settling up. Sammi asked us to take care of you, said the Realms hadn't been kind to you of late. They'll be here tomorrow night and apologize for not being here. They had to make an emergency run and all. There’s a bed upstairs. When you're ready just grab me and I'll take you up. You can get food here in the morning. Now I need to get back to it. If you need anything just wave me over..." With a smile she was gone back into the crowd.

Kali sat back in the comfortable chair and sipped the thick, rich, dark liquid, full of hidden flavor and the subtle hints of an ageless tradition of brew making. Thoughts whirled around in confusion. Thoughts of where she had come from, questions of how she had arrived, and questions about what to do next. Should she be angry or frightened by the taking of her? As she sat and sipped stout she decided not. Nothing had been holding her to Seattle and she had always wanted an adventure. Besides, the final choice had been hers.

Shaking her head to clear it she raised a hand and waved Jo over. She raised her mug and looked at it longingly before smiling. "Another coming right up." Jo answered her silent plea.

"Got a moment?" Kali asked as Jo spun the new mug onto the table.

"Sure. You want to know how it all works and how you got here."

"Yes...?"

"It’s the most asked of course. This place exists outside the Realms. It is our commission to rescue the beauty and art of the places in the Realms when destruction threatens it. That’s the easy part. None of us know exactly how we are chosen and transported to here."

"I was..."

"Shhh, it is not asked nor is it answered except among close friends. The Lady determines and selects, that's all any really know of it. How’s the beer and food? You doing ok otherwise? Sammi and Jemima can maybe fill in a little more for you tomorrow."

"I was thinking I'd finish this drink and free up the table."

"Take your time. There are a few tables in here that are always waiting for certain people. This is one. The large group in the center is for the Temple Heath crowd. They're here every night, as are the Central Station people over there." She waved first to a loud happy group in the center of the room and then to a smaller group across from them. "This table is always here for Sammi, Jemima, and now you if you'd like." Jo stood and returned to the bar while Kali looked around the room again.

She slowly finished her second stout then motioned Jo over again. "I think I'd like to fall into that bed now, if you don't mind..."

"Ok, follow me." Once again Jo threaded them through the pressing the common room, stopping to chat with this or that person along the way. At last she guided Kali through an almost hidden door in one of the support columns. She led the way up the narrow spiral stair inside, down a short hall, pointing to a door and saying, "Washroom," then stopping in front of another door a little farther on.

Inside was a small room tucked in under the eaves. Lacy curtains covered a small window and a fire burned in the grate chasing the chill from the room. A large bed sat below the window with its covers turned back. "Sleep well Kali. I'll see you in the morning."


The morning sun roused her as it spilled in through the curtains. Blinking sleepily she tried to remember where she was. It came back to her as she pulled the curtains aside to see a small garden below. Smiling she slipped out of bed and prepared to face the day.

She had expected the pub to be empty, instead most of the tables were filled with people eating. She ended up back at Sammi and Jemima's table in the vault. A server approached soon after she was seated with a menu and water. She ordered and watched the vault rapidly fill with people as she ate.

Fortified by a hearty pub style breakfast she stepped out into the early morning sunshine. The cathedral drew her eye as the morning light rendered it even more beautiful. She stood for long moments admiring it. Reluctantly she turned away and made her way to the street. She began to walk, drawn by something she couldn't identify. As she walked she realized how quiet the city was. Bird song, bicycle bells, and scraps of conversation drifted past her. There were no automobile sounds or smells and she didn't see any parking lots crowding up against the cathedral.

Just past the cathedral, on the inland side of the street, she saw a dark, brooding building crouching at the point of a triangular block. Her gaze was drawn by the heavy stonework and intricate carvings on its face. A small sward of overgrown grass lay between the street and the doors. A cracked walkway cut through the grass, leading from the street to the closed doors.

Curiosity pulled her up the broken and twisted walk to the yellow tape spider-webbed across the carved wooden doors. She could still make out the faded black letters of, "Crime Scene - Do Not Cross". Large brass lion handles glowered at her from behind the tape and stone gargoyles stared down from the roof above. Quiet waiting oozed from the building both pulling and repelling her. She slowly reached through the tape and pulled the left door. It squealed open on rusty hinges. Hesitantly she entered, almost as if the building had to reach out and drag her in.

Dusty colored light fell from a stained glass window high overhead illuminating a circle of orange cones with more yellow tape. Other pools fell on the wide stone stairwell clinging to the walls of the open circular atrium. The hand of the building pulled her more strongly now. She walked to the steps and began climbing. By the time she reached the top she was almost running. She skidded into the fourth floor hallway and stopped confused.

Higher, she had to get higher. Searching she finally found the small oak door with a rose covered ankh carved into it. It opened to a narrow, circular, wrought iron stairway that drew her higher. Scrambling, almost falling in her haste she clawed her way up and into an ante-room. To her left was a circular room almost completely covered in windows. In front of her was an open space and then another wrought iron circular staircase rising to a higher floor. To her right was a hall leading off in two directions and a door.

The view of the cathedral drew her into the circular room. Brightly colored throw pillows covered most of the rich Oriental rug centered in the room. Near the edges she could just see the hardwood floor underneath. A large, deep easy chair was pulled up to the windows and placed so it had a perfect view of the cathedral. An ornate chandelier hung over it with its wicks ready for the night.

Still the need to go higher pulled her back to the stairs. They emerged into a round tower room, above the rest of the roof line and completely surrounded in windows. A huge four poster bed dominated the room, it’s blood red velvet curtains drawn back to reveal the black bed spread with a single red rose embroidered on it. It’s uprights and crosspieces were intricately woven wrought iron traceries. Lace curtains framed the windows while thicker ones brooded between them, waiting to close out the light, or hold it in at night. Toward the back of the building were patio doors leading out onto a small balcony.

A teak wardrobe stood to the side of the stairs and a large trunk crouched at the foot of the bed. The cavern of the wardrobe barely noticed the meager stock of clothing within. A black cat suit hung next to three dark green flight suits, two pairs of jeans, and a couple of folded t shirts rested on the shelf. A worn pair of motorcycle boots with metal shin guards stood propped in a corner.

The trunk was also nearly empty, holding only a small oilskin pouch with a well crafted set of lock picking tools, a coil of climbing rope and a small bag of pitons with a hammer.

The patio doors opened onto a small balcony that overlooked the roof line of the building. It looked down on a triangular section of roof that had been made into a garden. One either side were doors into the wings of the building that attached to the lower circular room she had just left.

The need to explore the rest of the area dragged her away from the views and back down to the hallway. Halls led off to the left and the right. The door swung open to reveal a sky lit bathroom with an enormous claw footed tub. Ivy wove itself around the windows above the tub and up to a latticework near the skylight. She could just make out the railing of the balcony above through the twined leaves. A thick forest green throw rug masked the orange, red, and brown tile of the floor. Under the dust, fluffy purple towels hung expectantly on a brass rail, waiting invitingly for the next bather. Beyond the window was the roof garden. Bright flowers bloomed in the early morning light and a small fountain played in the center of an open area.

Turning back to the passageways she turned left and rounded a corner. The left wall was a series of windows looking out into the garden area and part way down on the right was another door. She stopped and opened it. Across from her were more windows. Mirrors lined the other three walls and a waist high brass rail encircled the room. A small stereo stood on a wheeled stand in the left corner near the windows. An impulse moved through her and soon she was half dancing, half just moving around the room. Small clouds of dust puffed up from her feet as she slowly warmed up. Somehow her muscles knew how to move, far better than they ever had before. Even the stiffness in her left shoulder was less noticeable.

Once her glance fell across herself in the mirror and she cringed at her reflection. She hadn't realized just how much weight she'd gained over the last year. The pudgy baby face her mom had given her was even more noticeable than it had been. So was the added thickness around her middle. Just like her mom she stacked it on in her stomach rather than her hips and thighs. Quickly she turned so she was looking out the windows as she moved.

It took a while before curiosity pulled her out of movement and to the door at the end of the hall. Beyond it was a large study with an oak partners desk holding court in the room. The wall to her right was covered in bookshelves. The other three walls alternated between more shelves and windows revealing the garden, the back street, and the side street. The buildings beyond were slightly lower than the one she was in and showed jagged roof lines and intriguing oddities of angle. On the desk was a computer and keyboard. There was a door near the one she entered through that led to the garden.

She crossed to it and stepped into the garden area. She wandered among the plants for a while, marveling at how healthy they were even though they showed signs of neglect. Someone had put a lot of work into the arrangement and taken good care of them. There was another door, almost directly across from the study, that opened into a cavernous kitchen. A large brass rack hung from the ceiling in the center of the room supporting trailing ivy and large kitchen utensils. Beneath the rack was a butcher-block central island with a knife rack mounted on the side. An industrial size gas stove dominated the wall to her right and was backed by windows facing the road behind the building. On the wall to her left was an enormous icebox standing next to a door. On it was a poster of a ballet dancer in mid movement and the phrase, "Eat Right, Respect Your Body, Dance Forever". The door opened onto a hallway leading back into the rest of the apartment. It passed an empty room and emerged on the other side of the bathroom.

Normally she would tell everyone she wasn't the cleaning type, in fact she'd sum herself up as ‘domestically impaired’, but there she was, scrubbing that place for all she was worth. She couldn't have told anyone why, it was more of a compulsion than anything else. Most of the day passed as she swept, scrubbed, dusted, and straightened. At last she collapsed on the pillows in the living area.


It was dark when hunger woke her. Only a few lights were visible from her windows, along with the glow of Central Station in the distance. A feature of the city she remembered from John’s descriptions. She prepared herself for a long, groping descent through the dark stairwells of the building, but when she stepped back into the gloom it seemed less dark than it should have been. In no time at all she had reached the street and had turned her steps toward the Adam and Eve and food.

Jo guided her to the table near the fire then returned with a huge plate of food and a Murphy’s Imperial. As Jo turned to go Kali asked her how she could find out who owned a place, blushing all the while. "Why, did you find something you like?"

Nodding excitedly she replied, "There’s this wonderful place near the cathedral, but it looks like no one has been there in a very long time. I'd like to find the landlord, or someone who could tell me more about it."

"Big Joe knows the most about the places around here. I'll send him over in just a bit."

Soon Big Joe wandered over and settled in. "You're going to stay then?"

"Uh..." His question caught her off guard. "I, yeah, I thought I'd stay. I guess, I mean, do I have to go back? I hoped I could stay."

"You could, yes," A strange look flickered across his face so fast she wasn't sure she actually saw it. "As Sammi explained it to us, you were given a chance to visit. You are free to go back any time."

Panic clawed its way up her throat as she thought again of her boring endless future in the Realms. "Do I have to go back? Could I stay and see if I like it here?"

"Certainly you can stay. The Lady won't turn you away, else she wouldn't have let you come in the first place. Now I hear you've been out looking for a place. What’s the matter? Isn't our hospitality good enough for you?"

She started and stuttered until she saw the twinkle in his eye and the grin spreading over his face. "Umm, it’s wonderful...it’s just...well, I've seen this place that’s even more wonderful, it’s perfect, and I'd like to know who owns it."

"And were is this ‘dream spot’?"

"In the building by the cathedral, the one with the police tape..." she slowed to a stop as she saw his face grow thoughtful.

"I don't believe I know that one. Were is it again?"

"It’s right across from the cathedral, just down the street from here. It’s not hard to spot, it’s the tallest building around except for the cathedral."

"Could you describe it for me?"

She began to try and describe it in words, "triangular, sort of, it fills the lot between the two roads leading away from the cathedral, beautiful gothic stonework surrounds the main entry foyer, which is in the point of the triangle. Inside is a large entry area with a circular stairwell going up and stained glass windows throwing rich colors on old marble..." she paused, trying to conjure up the picture of it in her head.

Joe watched her with a strange look as she struggled for the words. "What did you do before you came here?"

"Huh, what?" Concentration broken she stared at him. "Why?" Puzzled by his intense and serious look she started, "I programmed computers, fixed broken electronic things, wrote.."

"You wrote...?" he said stunned.

"Well, not to be published really, more as a way of getting at things in my head. Why?" He collapsed into the chair across from her looking pale.

"Writers have more power here than most. They can make things happen, even if they normally might not." It was her turn to look afraid. "No, it’s no where near omnipotence or anything like that, but things Change when Writers are around, a Writer can have great influence over non critical things. For example I'd be willing to bet you brought that building here. The spot you are talking about used to be a row of small houses. No one lived there. They were just what was nearby. I wouldn't worry about moving in, it’s yours, you called it."

She reached a shaky hand toward her stout, then took a long pull and sat back, stunned. A train whistle sounded far in the distance, "If you have more questions ask Sammi or Jemima, I think that’s their train, just wait to be sure they haven't had a hard time this trip..." He was recovering quickly, "Oh, one other thing, you'll end up looking like you see yourself in your dreams here. It'll be especially true for you, just remember that..."

Chills still chased through her nerves, "Could you have Sammi and Jemima’s favorite drinks here waiting for them? I seem to recall it was Newcastle?"

"That’s right, coming right up, Ms. Writer!" he gave her a shaky grin, beginning to recover from his shock.

After he left she chewed on what he'd said, vowing quietly to be very careful from now on. The thoughts of the previous night returned to chase through her mind again. Big Joe’s revelations added to the sense of stepping into a weird dream and not being certain it wasn't really a nightmare, thinly disguised as pleasant. She was well into her second Murphy’s by the time the door opened and two women walked in. It wasn't until they stopped, looked, and headed her way that she knew they were Sammi and Jemima. She sat and waited uncertainly as they approached.


part - Meetings

She saw them stop, stare, then continue toward the table. Suddenly the one in the back grinned and shoved her companion ahead of her. "Kali, well here is a welcome surprise! Oi!" The last bit was directed at Sammi who was still trying to distinguish Kali’s features in the flickering firelight. "Come on love, she’s even got the beers in for us - and after what we've been through I think we could both do with a drink or three." She said as she guided Sammi over to the table and pushed her into the seat opposite Kali.

Sammi seemed to come back to herself as Jemima pushed one of the bottles into her hand. "Don't mind me...I...I mean we - that was a bad one. But," she said as she took a long pull from her beer, "we survived. Come, love", turning to Jemima, kissing her gently on the cheek, "they say a pain shared is a pain halved - shall we talk about it?"

Jemima took a long drink of her own, then reminded Kali to do likewise, "Hey, come on, if we two are going to get sozzled and pour our hearts out to you, the least you can do is return the favor - Cheers!" Another long pull drained her bottle and she immediately waved to Jo for another.

Kali took another deep drought of her Imperial Stout. While she was still savoring it Jo flitted over a tray with three more drinks, expertly sliding them within easy grasp of the three at the table. With a flourish of her black skirt she was off again to check on the other patrons.

Jemima looked at Sammi who was gazing into the fire and said, "She’s had a hard trip. In fact we both have. Just now I think we both need to talk a few things over, at least you should get an interesting tale out of it!" Jemima paused for a long time before she began, "It was a hard mission. We had gone out as a standard recovery mission to a world where the dark side involvement was higher than normal. We had finished our mission and were headed back when we received word that one of the other teams had been captured. As a result we ended up becoming an Extraction Team without any warning or preparation." She took a long shaky sip from her beer. "By the time we arrived back the other team had been taken to one of the temples and were being prepared as sacrifices to the Dark Ones. Sometimes...sometimes there is no way to...sometimes the only rescue that can be performed is to send a team member into death to release them from the demonic forces. This was one of those missions. Most of the others were lucky. We found them caged outside the temple, all except Kerith."

Jemima paused again and reached out to lay her hand to Sammi's shoulder. For a long moment they just gazed at each other, a stream of love and affection seeming to flow between them, then Jemima resumed the tale. "Kerith is dead and need never fear suffering again. You were right about those bastards", She nodded at Sammi, "when we smashed through the barrier they had her staked out on the altar, naked, and the vermin were pushing red hot needles into her skin. That wasn't the worst of it, though, that black priest was there, and had her mind in some kind of torment - as we raced down the nave she must have heard the noise of the engine, for she looked towards us with all of Hell in her eyes". Sammi flinched and tears ran unchecked from her eyes, remembering how she’s had to wait at an outlying spot. She had held the counter spell up so the others could get through to the temple.

"At least she is beyond their reach now", Sammi fought the words round the cold lump in her throat, "but to think she died like that -"

"No. No!" Jemima interrupted, finally realizing what had upset Sammi so for the last two days, "Megren gave us a perfect approach, old "Shergar" rolled right up on the altar and cut poor Kerith in half - but while demonic magic ends instantly, life takes a second longer. I was leaning from the leading window, and just for a second, while we thundered forward, she was freed of her pain", Jemima gazed intently into Sammi's eyes as she went on, "Never in my life have I seen such bliss on a human face, I swear she found the havens there in front of my eyes! Her death was a release, not a torment."

For long moments it seemed that Sammi didn't hear what Jemima was saying, the relief washed through her and she threw herself into her lover’s arms. "She really died in peace?" Sammi asked, as the pain faded realizing Jemima would never lie to her.

"She died in peace, with 55055 running down her torturers", Jemima answered.

"What happened next?" Sammi asked, after a long moment.

"Shergar rammed the tabernacle and all of hell erupted around us", Jemima answered, "I was still at the window, and I saw the temple engulfed in magic fire just as I was thrown to the floor. Then something, with the power of death itself, grabbed hold of the train. I came to where you found me, scorched and smoking".

Sammi took up the story, "We were supposed to back them up. Get them out if anything went wrong. So we followed along about twenty minutes behind them in one of the steam freight trains. Where the temple had been we found only a shattered wasteland. Beyond the still smoldering bits and pieces we found Shergar, stopped and smoking. Every last bit of paint had been burned away. The carriages were wrapped in smoke. When we entered we found blackened smoldering figures collapsed on the floor. It was the most awful thing I have ever seen. None of them looked as if they could possibly be alive. It was only as they began to struggle back to consciousness that we realized how lucky they had been. There were minor burns and injuries where people had bounced off the carriage sides as everything went up. Megren was the worst with second degree burns over all her exposed skin from where she was in the engine. We hooked up to the other train and pulled it to the nearest depot for emergency repairs. After that Shergar was able to limp back here under her own power. And that's our tale", Sammi said as she sat back, relaxing at last, the last traces of tension draining from her face in the firelight.

They were still sitting after Sammi had finished her descriptions. Jemima was reliving parts of it, Sammi was still locked in the images of the aftermath, and Kali was seeing fragments of it. As they shook their heads, trying to clear the images, a band entered and began setting up. Something about them seemed very familiar to Kali, like she should know them from somewhere. After a few moments the lead singer turned and she could see her. "That's not Inkubus Sukkubus over there, is it?"

"It most certainly is", Jemima grinned back at her, "I trust you can dance?" she added, laughing eyes smiling at her above her tankard.

She grinned back, trying not to let the clawing fear show in her face. The old familiar patterns of it began to build in her, but the music was so infectious that it began to ease a bit. Soon she was swaying and moving in her seat to the power of the music swirling around the room.

When the second song began she suddenly found herself on her feet moving and swirling among the other dancers. Softly it slipped into her mind, driving the fear out and slowly becoming the focus of her every thought. At first her movements were stiff and awkward, but as the music slowly worked its way into her she could feel her joints popping and loosening like cracking the ice on fall puddles to reveal the water, still fluid, underneath.

The music wove a bright shimmering pattern in her head that her feet were compelled to follow. Surprise flared briefly that she could dance at all then the music drove itself back to the center. Her random and disjointed movements slowly coalesced into a woven tapestry of cat like grace and flow. She became obsessed with matching the ethereal pattern she could sense only dimly. Then it happened, like stepping through a doorway. The pattern flared into three-dimensional brilliance and everything became one. There was no Kali, there was no music, no pub, no band, no people, just the dip and flow of the pattern. Within it was the peace and completeness she'd longed for all her life. For an instant she saw windows and doorways into the past, the future, the now, saw what she had only imagined as she had tried to write of racial memories, of pasts back to the beginnings of time.

There was no sense of time or space until the music slowly faded away and the silence brought her back to the pub. Without a thought she bowed deeply to the band, then the thunder of applause rolled over her. It was only then she noticed everyone else had drawn back into a circle to give her room to dance. Panic surged through her as she realized she had been the center. Her gaze flicked and darted as she sought a way to safety. As her eyes darted across the gaze of the lead singer, the singer saw her, laughed, and launched into "Wytches". Suddenly the pattern surged and beckoned once more.

Sammi grabbed one hand as Jemima grabbed the other. Soon everyone was linked in a circle snaking and turning through the pattern. For a time she held back a bit, enjoying the contact with new friends, then as the band shifted into another song she let go and returned to the pattern. Too soon it was over. Exhausted, they staggered back to their table. Soon Jo had brought pints of water. Gratefully they sipped them and slowly regained their breath.

The promise of a hot bath drew her when she arrived home. She discovered one of the joys of being a Writer was not having to wait for hot water, even on the top floor of a building. Within moments she was curled up in her tub, relaxing in the lightly jasmine scented water. When the water had cooled to discomfort she pulled herself out, dried off, and made her way to bed.

As she lay there the oddity of Inkubus Sukkubus drew her attention again. The more she thought about them the more she wondered how had they been at the bar. That led to wondering if they had been shifted like she had, or if they were an echo of their presence elsewhere. Which led into wondering if a Writer had Written them there. Here she was a Writer and yet she was also a character in what was being Written. It did seem to fit, in an odd sort of way, as she realized she had always been a watcher who would sometimes participate. Her next thoughts were more disturbing. She began to wonder if the Story had come to have a life of its own. She guessed it must have, at least on some level. Was that level enough to sustain it if she or Jack died. She didn't know and hoped she wouldn't have to find out.

She was reminded of a theory a gaming friend of hers had once mentioned. It stated that gods were created by the beliefs of their followers. The more followers, the more power, the more influence on ‘reality’. Maybe it worked the same with Written worlds. After all, words were symbols linked in patterns, and reality was patterns. Maybe, she thought, the old alchemists had it right when they said power resided in words - words as symbols. Other thoughts struggled to intrude but sleep pulled her down before they formed.


She awoke the next morning refreshed, quickly dressed, and headed off to meet Sammi and Jemima for breakfast. They laughed and carried on over huge amounts of food. At last she asked the question that had been on her mind during most of the meal, "Umm, I'm still not too certain what I should be doing, and I need to be doing something...I don't want to feel like a parasite here...and I know I told Jack I wanted to visit. Now that I'm here I don't want to go back."

"We thought you might not want to. He was sure you would. What are you good at, besides dancing?"

"Well, I'm good with technical things. If I can get it apart I can usually get it back together and working...I am also good with computers..."

"You know, you might go check at the train yards, last I heard they were needing more help. If you don't mind getting dirty it might be fun."

"I think I'd enjoy that, although I'd like to go on some of the rescue assignments also..."

"Don't worry, almost everyone here goes at some point or another, some only the minimum number they can get away with. Some of us can't live without the excitement...even though there is great danger. Since it is the reason Death City exists it is a requirement that all residents participate in rescues once in a while..but enough for now...we can talk about that later..."

Soon Sammi and Jemima were finished and hurried off to their appointments. Kali set out, past the pub, toward the dark river, running silent through the city. Following the path she passed through a gate, out of the cathedral lands and then along the river walk until it passed under the great railroad bridge a bit further down stream. There she climbed a set of worn stone stairs up to the rail bed and crossed the river. Once across it was a short walk near the track to the Temple Heath Locomotive Depot. A couple of different people pointed her in the direction of one of the running sheds and Bartholomew, whom everyone called Bart, the man in charge.

She knew she was in the right place as soon as she opened the personnel door on the side of the huge old building. The warm scent of diesel oil, mixed with old smoke and lubricating oils rolled over her. She was so busy inhaling deeply and savoring the smells to notice the stares she was getting. Just as a man near the door started to ask her what she wanted she walked over to him and asked after Bart.

He answered, "Over near Shergar, he’s checking her after last night’s excitement. Why?"

"I heard he was looking for techs, um I don't think I know the right term.." She replied blushing under his scrutiny.

He looked her up and down a few times before pointing across the building to an older diesel electric locomotive. "He’s over there, in the large group of people near the engineer’s position."

"Thanks." She could feel his eyes on her as she crossed to the large knot of people. Conversation slowed at her approach, finally stopping as she asked, "Hi, I was looking for Bart? I wanted to talk with him about a maintenance position, but I can come back at a better time..."

"I'm Bart, and nonsense young lady, this is a fine time. We were just rambling on about old Shergar and all she’s seen. Come with me a moment and we'll get you fixed up." He was huge and resembled the locomotives under his care. Tall and wide with a barrel chest and arms that looked as big as her thighs. Suddenly she wasn't so sure about this. She began to remember the pictures of locomotives she'd seen, most everything in them came in sizes large to huge.

By the time they reached his office she was having serious second thoughts. Just as she was about to apologize and slip quietly away Bart spoke. "I guess I should ask what your credentials are. What have you worked on? What background do you have?" At her dismayed look he just grinned and added, "None is really required, other than a willingness to get dirty, to learn, and to work hard, but I would like to know what you've done before now..."

She could see his opinion of her change as she described her experience, especially the time she spent as a seismic field service technician. "Good, we can use someone that understands that computer stuff and who can work under difficult conditions. Several of the latest locomotives have ‘microprocessor’ control systems in them. If you can start today I can assign you to the checkout of Shergar, that'll let you see how the older diesel-electrics work. She’s a good old one she is. It looks like she’s ok, but we wouldn't want her to quit in the middle of a run. Go over to the locker rooms and grab yourself a pair of dungarees and meet me back by her."

Soon he was showing her oil points, valves, controls, pistons, vents, and numerous other things she was sure she wouldn't remember for many weeks. "Got all that? I'll test you on it tomorrow," he said with a grin. "It'll take time, but not as much as you expect."

She only worked half the day but still it was enough to exhaust her. Her arms felt like limp noodles from all the lifting, pushing, pulling and twisting that she'd done, but there was a great deal of satisfaction too. She couldn't remember when working had felt so good.

She hurried home, changed and headed for the Adam and Eve, trying to remember if Sammi and Jemima were going to join her that night.


She was headed for Sammi’s table when Bart’s voice stopped her. "Hey Kali, don't be a stranger, come sit with us." She quickly spotted Bart at the tables grouped in the center of the room. Cheeks flaming, embarrassed by the attention, she hastily made her way to an empty chair. "You're one of us now, for good or ill," Bart continued with a huge smile. He turned and waved at Jo, "Bring Kali one of her usuals, would you? Thanks."

Kali’s stout had just arrived when Sammi walked in and headed toward her table. She looked around for a few moments before she spotted Kali. "So, already abandoning your friends for these guys?" she asked smiling. "Hey Bart, how’s the loco?"

"Not nearly as bad as you had me believing you scamp. Where’s your better half?"

"Setting it up so Kali can ride in the cab with us to Portal Station tomorrow. Why?"

"Just thought she should be keepin’ an eye on you is all."

"You! Kali, watch out for that one. He’s trouble."

"So, she just starts at the yards and already you're taking her away. It’s a wonder I can get anything done around here." He turned and winked at Kali. "Just remember, the longer you keep her, the longer it'll take to get your locomotive back."

Sammi was about to reply when Jemima burst in and started toward them. "Got it!" She said, waving a scrap of paper in one hand. She pulled Sammi into a tight hug before turning to Kali and continuing, "Tomorrow morning you get to go to Portal Station with us in the cab of the loco."

"Pull up a couple of chairs and join us."

"Yes sir, mister Bart, sir." Jemima answered with a smile as she grabbed a chair and spun it to the table. Sammi quickly settled into one of her own and they spent the rest of the evening in pleasant conversation.


As Jemima rose to leave she turned to Kali, handed her the cab pass, and said, "Meet us at Central Station at sunrise with the permit."

Muscles protested as Kali stood. She stifled a groan and waved at the table, "See you guys later. I'm home for bed." She slowly made her way home and labored up the stairs to her rooms, where she quickly started a hot bath, after dropping a generous amount of bath salts into the tub. As the steam rose, she stripped and sank slowly into the rising water. Soon she was drifting through half formed thoughts as the heat loosened her tired muscles.

Tired and finally pain free she slipped into bed and drifted right into sleep. The next thing she remembered was the full moon shining into her room. It must have been the middle of the night, yet it seemed almost as bright as day. Worse, she was wide-awake. She lay there for long minutes, willing herself to sleep again. At last she gave it up and climbed out of bed.

She wandered the room for a while until the pull of the moonlight became too much. Hurrying to her wardrobe she pulled out the cat suit, saw how tightly it would fit, and threw it in the back corner. She pulled on a flight suit instead. As she turned to the stairs, the doors and the balcony above her garden, caught her eye. In seconds she had slipped onto the balcony and from there onto the slope of the roof. She waited for the fear and vertigo that had followed her most of her life to overwhelm her once again. It whispered in the back of her mind, but didn't come forward very far. After waiting a few minutes she prowled along the left ridge line to the end of the building. There was a three-foot gap and a ten-foot drop between her roof and the next one over. Looking over to the end of the right ridge line showed the same three-foot gap and a drop of 8 feet. Frustrated she stalked back to the windows and headed down into the building.

Her hand was on the main doors when she remembered the horrible squeal it would make if she opened it. Not wanting that level of noise she slipped deeper into the building. A hallway led down the left side it and ended at a door. Carefully she turned the knob. This door opened on silent hinges and let her out into the narrow canyon between her building and the ones behind it. Here and there shapes huddled in the deeper shadows. A closer look revealed people under blankets and in large coats. They had to be street people, but they didn't look quite as beaten down as the ones she was used to. The clothes they wore were somewhat clean and in reasonable repair and they didn't smell like they feared water and soap.

She started toward the street when she heard a large group approaching, probably from the Adam and Eve. Quickly she ducked back into the alleyway, only to be brought up short as a woman’s voice said, "Ye need not fear them. Ye be safe in Death City and in all Eternia from the rest of us. It be only yourself ye need fear."

Startled, Kali snapped out, "What do you know of me?"

"Ye be one of the rare ones. Ye walk the shadow line by choice, that be why ye have the hand of the Dark Mother on ye. Ye did not die to come here. Your transition is a different one, it be of flesh and spirit. Yet e’en so, ye be less than comfortable in yer skin."

"Shadow walker, fence rider, great, another place where I'm too much in the center to be valid. What gives you the right to judge me?!?" she spat out, her face twisted into a sneer by bitterness.

"Ye don't understand, do ye girl? Here Shadow Walkers have a place. Ye walk between worlds here, as ye walked between extremes in the realms. This is the place between, a place where the tasks of salvation and rescue are taken seriously. Balance and center are very important. Here those that understand Between have the best time of it. Here ye be judged only by how ye aid those around ye and ye be safe from all but yourself. Beyond these borders though, that be a different matter. The forces of evil will seek to destroy ye, to prevent ye thwarting them. The forces of good may walk over ye, confusing ye with the evil uns. Always the Dark Mother watches over, she who was before the Others. But here I'm chattering on like some crazy magpie and ye be cold of spirit. Go, find yer peace. Old Lizbet be here when ye want to talk again girl. This alley be my home."

Strangely calmer Kali made her way to the front of her building where she could see the cathedral in all its glory. She didn't see the old woman shimmer and fade into the night. The cathedral drew her closer as she studied the flying buttresses and spires arrogantly poking into the heavens. As she neared the building she began to see small cracks and gaps in the stonework. Before she really thought about it she was climbing. Each new foothold spurred her hands to seek the next space. Slowly and steadily she worked her way up a buttress, across an arch and higher up along the roof line. Her fingers and feet seemed to know just where to go.

After an hour of steady climbing she reached the top of the highest spire. Wind whistled through her hair and the moon bathed her in silvery light. Something started to shift in her. The last terror of heights faded quickly before the light, wind, and stunning views. To the east and north the river curled it's way around the cathedral close. Very slightly to the north and east was the Adam and Eve, and to the south and west, Central Station, where she would join Sammi and Jemima in the morning. To the west was her building and another section of the city.

As the sun began to color the wispy clouds in the east she began the climb back down to the street, then figured what the hell and slid instead to the belfry. From there she boldly strode down the stairs and out onto the street, receiving a couple of startled looks from others in the cathedral, but otherwise no one said a word.

Soon she was out on the street and headed toward the path along the river. As she turned past the Adam and Eve she headed as if to Temple Heath. Once she reached the rail bed she turned away from the river and followed a pathway to the front of the station. She stopped in awe of the beauty of that massive old building. Victorian architecture soared skyward and massive sections of glass glistened in the coming light.


Journeys - Into the Void

Kali stood and admired the station as the sun climbed higher into the sky. At last she turned and entered. A quick flash of the cab permit from Sammi and the conductor waved her past, pointing toward the head of the train. She slowly walked toward the engines, stopping once and a while to admire the gleaming blue and gold coaches along the way. Soon she emerged from the traceries of the overhead glass and ironwork. She passed the last three coaches and reached the twin diesels, already idling in preparation for departure. Even at idle they radiated power and presence. Fascinated she walked slowly by them before stopping to lean against a nearby signal gantry. Sammi had told her this wasn't their normal train. Shergar and her coaches would be in the works for many weeks yet. Sammi had managed to wrangle a driving turn for the upcoming short trip to Portal Station. These locomotives were Class 37 diesel electrics, not the Napier Marine Deltic that Shergar was.

While she waited she looked around at the other platforms, watching the other trains arriving and departing. Railroad equipment from dozens of different countries, or worlds, were waiting or being serviced. It produced a wonderful riot of color and shape. Abruptly a short train roared away from the next platform, rapidly disappearing into the dawn brilliance across the rail bridge. As it vanished in the distance strong arms grabbed her from behind while Sammi’s voice asked, "What shall we do with this one then?"

She spun when Sammi released her and grabbed her new friends in a quick hug, "Bright greetings!"

"I suppose we'll have to take her with us." Jemima answered.

The sound of moving pulleys caught their attention as the signal above their heads changed to ‘Clear’. Sammi led the way to the lead locomotive and they scrambled aboard. Behind them there were shouted good-byes and sounds of slamming doors. Somewhere in the distance was a shouted, "Hey, wait for me!" Followed by an answering, "Hey, Kyrnan, can't you ever be on time?"

Sammi moved to the driver’s seat and motioned Kali to the other chair while Jemima moved behind Sammi and settled her hands on her shoulders. Sammi unlocked the controls and activated the warning devices. Kali watched with intense interest as Sammi went through each step of departure. A whistle blew in the distance, which Sammi answered with a short blast from the horn as she released the brake. With a jaunty grin she eased the power controller open. There was a slight lurch as the traction motors took up the load. With a snarl the locomotives began to ease forward. Like a waking beast it slowly gained speed as it clawed its way down the track.

"Kali, Stick your head out and have a listen", Sammi called over the rising roar of the engines, "I'm going to thrash this one!" Jemima reached over and opened the cab side door near her while Kali and Sammi opened the windows near them. Leaning out, as the slow moving train cleared the end of the platform, Kali could see the varnished coaches smoothly gliding along behind. Sammi opened her controller a bit more, now the two Class 37s really began to roar, and Kali felt the train surge forward. With a clatter of wheels on joints they were on the river bridge, glancing back into the cab Kali could see the Cathedral spire through the open door beyond Jemima.

Jemima’s eyes were shut as she drank in the singing of the diesels. Sammi kept the regulators set just below the maximum limits as they roared along. Power sang through the floor and chair that Kali sat in. She leaned out the window again and reveled in the whipping wind. Soon they thundered through open park land and then over a small rise and down through an industrialized valley. It took only moments to rush through the brick lined cuttings, under plate girder bridges, and back out into the warm sunlight.

As their speed passed sixty, Kali pulled her head back out of the brutal wind. Her gaze drifted to her new friends. Jemima was leaning close to Sammi, stroking her shoulders while one of Sammi’s hands rested on hers. They almost glowed with the love they shared. Suddenly Sammi looked at her and winked, letting her know they had been aware of her gaze.

Sammi reluctantly shut the power down when their speed reached eighty. The engines dropped back to the low rumble of their idle as the train coasted along at eighty-two miles per hour. Other routes branched off to the right and left with growing frequency. The main line had increased to four tracks and was running under an elaborate overhead signaling system. Kali could make nothing of them but Sammi seemed to know exactly what they were saying.

Soon the four main lines increased to six and Sammi smoothly eased over to the right hand pair of lines. They were running through what looked like the industrial zone of a large Victorian working city. Factories, mills, and brick works stood along the lines and canals and wagon ways wove a tight web tying the rest of the city to the tracks. Ahead, on a hill rising higher than the chimneys and warehouses, were buildings of white stone, surrounded by spaces of green. The four left most lines headed toward it, curving slightly to the left, then running straight into a gradually deepening cutting. The twin tracks they were on branched to the right and ran through a valley of rock walls, swinging away from the city center and arrowing toward the distant mountains.

Sammi pulled the controller wide open again as they cleared the city junctions and headed out into the suburban areas. Large houses with tree shaded lawns and gardens swept past while another junction brought two lines in from the city to join and form four lines again. Then they were climbing, here just gentle slopes that slowly brought them out of the green valleys and into the rolling foothills of the approaching mountains. Sheep placidly gazed at them as they roared by.

"Could I ask you about this place? About Death City and Eternia?"

"You can. What would you like to know?" Jemima replied.

"Why everyone is so reluctant to tell me about it. How I got here. Why I got here. How does this place work?"

"Truth is they aren't being guarded on purpose, it's more that most of us don't know much. The Dark Lady determines who comes here and she hasn't told any of us how she decides. She arranges the way you get here as well. Again it's different for everyone and it is sort of a hard thing for most to talk about. There's usually loss and pain when it happens. As for how this place works, well, that's a bit simpler. Everyone has a desire to contribute, so they find things they don't mind doing and then they do them. You've met Big Joe and Jo, they enjoy running the Adam and Eve. Bart likes to work on the trains. And so it goes. We like the rush of missions, so we are out most of the time. It varies from person to person. It is expected that you will go out once in a while, but if you don't like it, you don't have to do it very often."


An hour later they were clinging to the side of the Mountains of Chaos. The four lines ran along a narrow ledge of stone blasted from the living rock of the towering mountains. Deep shadows blanketed the tracks, where the high peaks blocked the sun, and lent a dark mystery to the scene. The engines strained at maximum power rolling along at just under seventy-five. Narrow valleys and high waterfalls broke free in spots, one so close the spray left patterns on the wind screen. Moments later they screamed into a short tunnel, its walls throwing back the pulse of the engines. Immediately beyond the tunnel was a long span arching over a dizzying drop to a large river far below. Once again Kali was glad her fear of heights had faded. As they twisted and climbed higher the tunnels and bridges grew in numbers until they seemed to be alternately burrowing through the bones of the world and soaring through the heavens. Ahead, Jemima explained, lay the Great Portal, the main gate between Death City and Eternia and the rest of the universe. At the Portal lay Portal Station where Sammi would hand the train over to the regular crew who would take it into the void.

Abruptly the line swung around the shoulder of another mountain and Kali could see the Portal. Vast it was, huge and ancient, forged by the gods themselves in the ancient deeps before time began. Its boundary was a massive oval of metal, the color of age stained bronze. Within it was a pulsing, writhing something that no matter how hard Kali looked it wouldn't define itself. It pulsed with all colors and no color, at once a flat sheet of nothing and a view of everything that ever existed. As she stared at it she found herself drawn into it. Always feeling if she stared for a minute longer it would resolve itself into something.

"It's best not to look at it for too long". Kali started slightly as Jemima touched her shoulder. Kali's mouth formed a silent "Oh", as she gradually brought her mind back from the distant realms the Portal had carried her to. She was still aware of its vastness, towering above everything beyond the next range of mountains, but now she had recovered herself she would not again allow it to draw her gaze. Instead when she felt she just HAD to look at it, she would slip a sidelong glance its way, then quickly look back at something else.

"Sorry!" Sammi called above the roar of the engines, "we should have warned you. To be honest, it still freaks us out, and we've been here for years"

"That's ok", Kali responded, smiling across the cab at Sammi, "I'm glad I saw it. It's when you see things like that, things made not for mortal eyes, that you realize how precious a gift life is". Now the view of the Portal was being slowly cut off, as the train swung closer to the next range of mountains. On the other side, Jemima explained, was the Junction she'd spoken about, right at the edge of the Portal.

The chasm the line was following branched in two, and Kali found herself crossing an impossible bridge, a slender arch of lattice girders carrying the line right across the bottomless void below, then they were over and plunged into utter darkness. This final tunnel cut through the heart of the Mountains of Chaos. It was a four mile stretch of deepest black, cut through the living rock. Above it were the highest peaks of the range, one of the great barriers of Eternia. It threw back the sound of the diesels in ever increasing echoes until there was no escape from the pounding, crashing noise. Kali had never heard such sound before, on and on it went, amplified and boosted, nothing could escape from it.

As the pounding drove into her, she began to build a refuge of dance in her mind. As she danced her way deeper and deeper into the pattern a form began to take shape in front of her. Black as the void around the shining pattern, a necklace of skulls hung around her neck, the figure shimmered in front of Kali, ghostly, yet solid. Her voice blended in the echo of the roaring engines, "You have taken one of my names for your own. Yet you doubt yourself still. I gift you your word of power and I curse you to live the name you have chosen. You shall be as mother to your friends and as destroyer to your enemies. Your anger shall be quick and powerful, your love shall be boundless, yet the control of these sides shall be yours to master. You shall be remembered in the register of Death City - it is your choices that shall form the manner of that memory." Light flashed across her eyes, blotting out the vision as the train thundered out of the tunnel and began slowing to come to rest at the Portal Station.

She was still slightly dazed and disoriented as Sammi led her down from the cab and into the station to await their return. "Intense isn't it? It’s never become common for me! Now I don't know how long we'll have to wait. The Portal is always busy, but it could be some time before there’s room headed back."

Several trains came through during the next two hours, but they were all full of personnel or supplies. Shortly after yet another full train had slowly accelerated into the tunnel a voice boomed out over the announcement system, "Sammi, Jemima, Kali please come to dispatch."

Sammi shot the other two a puzzled look as they quickly walked to the door next to the information counters. Kali looked from her to Jemima and back and asked, "This isn't normal then?"

"No, usually we just wait until a train has space available and then get on." Sammi answered as she knocked on the door.

The door opened immediately to the cluttered office of the dispatchers. People were huddled in front of computer monitors displaying glowing traceries of lines and symbols. Beside each symbol was a name and number. As they entered a blond woman turned from her console as she pushed a hand through her already mussed and tangled hair. For a brief moment she just looked at Kali before saying, "We have a situation on Delestra 6 where the rescue mission has encountered heavy opposition. There is a team trapped under heavy fire. I need a small group to go in and set up an extraction. Try and get the train out. Failing that, set up a Rescue Beacon and Power Shield then dig in until we can get you. I'd like to send more people, but I don't have anyone close enough right now."

Sammi glanced at Jemima and quickly agreed. Then she turned to Kali and said, "If you want to come, you can, but no pressure. If you don't feel ready to jump into this high a danger, no one would have a problem with you declining."

Kali considered briefly then replied, "No, I'm here to make a difference. I'm not experienced yet, so if you think I would be a liability, then I'll stay, otherwise I'm in."

"Good! I have a train and driver waiting to go as soon as you board." She handed Sammi a large packet and continued, "This is all the information we have on the area. It was supposed to be a quiet zone so we didn't prepare for this. Good luck!" She then turned back to her console and keyed a couple of switches, then began talking softly into the headset she wore. With a grin and a wave to the room Sammi was bounding out. The other two followed almost as quickly.

They were met at the train by a long haired boyish looking man who Kali was certain she should recognize. "Welcome aboard!"

Once on board Sammi and Jemima took Kali to a weapons locker. Sammi pulled out a blaster rifle and handed it to her. "Have you ever used a gun before?"

"A pistol a couple of times with a friend of mine."

"Good, this isn't a lot different. Actually it should be easier, there’s no recoil to worry about. This is a MK986 heavy assault blaster. It can deliver one blast every two seconds and has a power pack good for 50 shots. It comes with an optional backpack assembly that boosts the number of shots to 1000. This particular one also has the add on grenade launcher attached. It holds five grenades and has a range of about 40 meters. It doesn't take long to get used to it and where we're going it sounds like there will be no trouble finding targets."

The train began moving as they dropped into nearby seats. Jemima snagged the packet and tore it open. Soon she had papers and maps spread out, covering a small table, and was intently studying what she found. Her finger traced a subway route then stopped under a large building. "This is where dispatch believes the team is right now. They were supposed to enter the subway system, then use it to access three additional locations. The last communication from the team indicated they had completed recovery operations on two of their three targets but were pinned down in the subway while trying to get to the third." Jemima pointed to another page of drawings and continued, "This is where they recommend we go in. Rather than risking getting trapped in the subways, we'll come in at the old train depot on the surface." She traced a small dotted line over to the first page. "Following this drain system should put us near the museum section of the tunnel. With any luck we won't have to fight our way through major forces until we reach the subway tunnels themselves. After that, we play it as it falls. Our main goal is to recover the team, after that we'll see what we can do."

"I don't understand, what is a Rescue Beacon? Can't they just send a train in the way the original team went in?" Kali asked.

"Normally yes, except the regular routes might take a long time to traverse. A Rescue Beacon allows dispatch to create a track route directly to the trouble spot. Help can arrive very quickly that way. A Power Shield is a magic device that raises a shield around an area. If we can't end the battle we can hide inside the shield until help arrives."

Almost too quickly a large thump and bang announced the train was back on real space track and slowing as it thundered through wrecked buildings and stacks of rubble. With a final hiss of brakes it rumbled to a stop in the center of a burned and tumbled shell of old stone and brickwork. Within moments they were standing away from the tracks as the train clawed its way into motion again. Quickly it accelerated down the tracks and roared through an opening in the far wall.

Sammi and Jemima were already settling their packs and gear as Kali turned from watching the departing train, still trying to remember why the driver had looked so familiar. Then it came to her, she had seen that same picture on a web page. He was Jack, the other Writer. With a grin she turned and joined Sammi and Jemima, adjusting her pack and blaster as she walked.

It took some searching to find the stairs down under all the rubble in the main areas. Then it took more time to slip and crawl over and around it to the old subway passages below. By the time they reached the lower platform they were covered in old soot, ash and cement powder. At first the going was easy as they followed the old passages to the subway station located below. Then they pulled up a large grate and dropped into the storm drains. For about 20 meters it was dry and easy then it turned and angled down. Slime and oil covered the bottom of the tunnel as it descended to meet a larger pipe. Here there was a thick floor of viscous mud and water.

The tunnel slanted down a ways further until they were wading through thick water or thin mud. Sammi grinned at Kali and commented, "This would be fun at any other time! Well, except for the stench. Right now it’s just a nightmare." About 500 meters along this tunnel Jemima motioned to the left and up a short ladder to a smaller tunnel. Single file they climbed up and into it, crouching as they went to avoid the lower curve of it.

The unease started slowly with a prickling at the back of Kali's neck. As they silently crept single file through the tunnel she found her hands tightening up on the blaster she carried. Eyes seemed to stare at her from the blackness around them and every sound seemed more and more ominous. Insecurities whispered to her of failure and death. Heart pounding she focused on Sammi in front of her and tried to ignore her rising panic. Her hands were beginning to hurt from clenching her blaster when Jemima signaled a halt at the last ladder up. She scrambled up for a look then trained her blaster on an old, rusty lock. It took only one shot to destroy it.

No surprise attacks greeted them as slipped into the tunnel above. They passed a side branch and another curve before Jemima held up her hand to hold. A reddish glow pulsed and throbbed from around the next bend. They could hear screams of pain and howls of rage broken every so often by the sound of weapons fire.

Softly they crept forward and rounded the bend. Grotesque lanky grey figures shrieked and gibbered as they threw themselves into the small knot of people huddled behind piles of rubble on the subway platform. Sporadic weapons fire would drive back the closest grey things and for a moment there would be a break then the grey things would close again. Sammi motioned at Jemima to take one side and for Kali to follow her into the other side.

For the first few seconds they had surprise and cut into the ranks of the grey beings. Then they turned and charged. Black bolts of energy leapt from a tall shape in the shadows of a stairway. It blasted a chunk of cement from the floor where Sammi had just leapt from. Kali froze as the mob of creatures rushed toward her. Then Sammi shoved her back yelling, "Snap out of it! Dance, damn it!!" A long narrow hand with razor claws ripped through the space where she had just stood. It was enough to break her loose. With an cat-like roar she spun and began firing back into the charging crowd. Twisting and dodging she kept herself out of danger while hurting her share of the enemy.

Suddenly the shadow spotted her and let loose with a wicked looking blast. In a move of pure desperation she dive-rolled over a fallen chunk of tunnel and heard an ominous crunching sound as she landed on her right shoulder. Sparks flashed from the damaged weapons pack on her back. Instinct drove her hands to the quick release on the straps as she dove away from it. A brilliant flash of heat and light told her how narrow her escape had been.

Now weaponless, she turned to retreat and saw Jemima knocked down by a glancing blow to her head. Something snapped inside her. An inhuman shrieking roar ripped through her throat as she hurled herself at Jemima’s attacker. Claws raked its throat out as she howled in triumph. Teeth pulled back in a snarling rictus of rage and feral joy she danced and wove her way through the left flank of grey beings. She left broken and bleeding corpses in a dark wake behind her. Teeth narrowly missed her and claws whistled around her as they tried to bring her down. Always she was just a fraction faster. Once she glanced back and saw Sammi, frozen, watching her. In a voice both terrifying and seductive she called, "Come, dance with me." The grey beings stopped and turned toward her, people started to rise from their covering locations, and Sammi walked toward her. The demonic forces shook off the thrall first and fired into the rising group of refugees, startling them into diving behind cover once more. Sammi blocked a blow by instinct, then shook her head and whirled back into the battle.

Kali continued her mad frenzy of destruction until a black blast shattered the floor at her feet. A howl of rage shredded her throat as she grabbed the nearest grey thing and hurled it into the stairs. It was still flailing as it slammed into the shadowy figure hiding there. She had a quick glimpse of a pulsing sparkle of light before slashing claws drew her back into the fray. Soon the entire left flank lay in bloody tatters at her feet. Still in a frenzy she spun seeking new targets and launched herself toward the nearest ones. As she drew back for a swing Jemima’s voice broke through, "Kali, it’s over. They're all dead. It’s over. We need to check the train and get a power shield readied before they bring in more."

As quickly as the frenzy had arrived, it departed. Kali was left standing and drained, with greenish blood, grey flesh, and ichor dripping from her curled fingers. It coated her clothes and clung to her skin. The smell of death slithered through the last of her adrenaline haze causing her to gag and retch. Confusion crossed her face as she croaked through her raw throat, "What happened? What have I done?"

"She touched you in the tunnel. The Lady touched you, didn't she?" Jemima asked.

"I...I think so...No...she did, I remember..." Kali whispered as they walked toward the other team.

Sammi had reached the other team and was making introductions as Kali and Jemima walked up. "Merris sent us to get you out of here. I am Sammi, this is Jemima, and this is Kali."

Jemima asked, "Where is your driver?"

"Tom is," A woman replied, pointing to a man where he sat cradling a broken arm.

"Are you able to drive?" He shook his head. "Anybody else know how?" The rest of them shook their heads no as well. She looked back Tom, "Do you think you could give Kali enough instruction that she could take the train out? We need to..."

"I can try..." Tom started to reply.

"We need to go. All of us." a woman broke in rapidly.

"Wha..." Tom started to say.

"Trust me," she said with absolute conviction. "We'll be cut off in minutes if we don't. Everyone, get the wounded on the train. We are leaving." She returned to speaking quietly into a com unit.

The team gathered their wounded and loaded them aboard. Tom stood shaking his head. "We aren't going anywhere. I was trying to tell you, the engine is damaged."

"Kali, think you could fix it?" Jemima asked. "Sammi and I can put up a shield in the passage before they come back. It should slow them down a bit."

"Maybe I can. Come on Tom." Tom trailed slowly after Kali as she hurried to the engine and disappeared on board.

The woman turned to one of her team mates, "Max, you're with me. The rest of you, whatever happens, don't let the train stop for anything."

"Take the Power Shield," Sammi called.

"No, you need it to block the passageway by the stairs, where you were going a minute ago." She hurried up the rail tunnel with Max following along behind. Sammi stared after her, shook her head, then headed toward the passage with the shield device.

Inside the locomotive Kali was peering into the smoke from the engine section. Taking a deep breath she plunged in. Hoses, wires, and pipes ran everywhere. Narrow spaces snaked and twisted their way through the packed equipment. Nothing looked too bad until she came to a junction box for the traction motor feeds. Melted copper, charred bakelite, and burnt insulation greeted her.

"Tom, are there any tools? I need a socket set and some really big pliers."

"Should be one in the back of the compartment. How's it look?"

"Bad. I may be able to cobble something together, I'll let you know." She reached for a melted section of wire then stopped. "Tom, how long would it take to start up again if we shut the diesels off? I don't want to get fried here."

"A couple of minutes. They'll still be pretty much warmed up."

"Good, would you please?" She waited until the engines wound down then began pulling on wires. Everything had been precisely installed, allowing for no slack. "I can make this work, but it will mean scavenging parts from the dynamic braking feeds. We will need to be really careful going down from Portal Station."

She worked rapidly cutting and joining, using scavenged connecting blocks and insulation pieces. At last she stepped back from the cobbled up mess. "Ok, start her up and lets see if this works."

The diesels slowly wound back to life. Everything seemed to hold together as Kali stepped back into the control cab. "Now, let's see if we can get out of here."

"Here, as driver you need to be in communication with the team lead." Tom picked up a com set from the control console. "There's a switch on the panel, there," he pointed to a selector, "That determines if you are talking to the train, the team wireless channel, or dispatch." Then he talked her through setting the Automatic Warning System. She cringed at the noise as it began to sound. She spun around and stabbed the cancel alert button before she even sat down. She dropped into the control chair and moved the reverser control lever to engine only and pulled the power handle towards her. The change in engine she expected didn't happen. Tom looked at her nervously, "That's not right. It should have responded immediately."

After a nervous glance out the windscreen she turned and climbed back into the engine compartment. Inside the compartment she could hear a ragged edge to the idling of the large engine next to her. As she moved toward the rear of the compartment she heard a faint hiss coming from the far side of the engine.
