"You caused quite a stir in Anastasia's group from what I heard tonight."

"Yeah, I guess. I couldn't just ignore what I saw. I had to be sure it wasn't real and when it was... How often do you see things that don't happen? How reliable is this likely to be for me, assuming it even happens again? In the Realms about half the time the impressions never happened."

"In the Realms mine were like yours, some would happen and some wouldn't. Here I have been right every time. They change if the sequence of events is modified, but, left without interference, they will play out as I see them, always."

"Oh..."

"Hey Kali," Ennui called from the door. "I thought you'd be sleeping after the mission. I hear you've been busy again."

"No shadows for me anymore," Kali responded bitterly. "Who's been talking? I thought everyone else would be resting."

"Natalya came in for a little while earlier. She was talking about a weapons cache and how you knew right where to go."

"She's seeing things," Dementia commented.

"Is she passing out, getting headaches, or other side effects?"

"Not that she's said. It sounds more like movements and placements rather than full on visions."

"No, she hasn't noticed side effects yet, thank you," Kali replied. "And she's still in the room."

"Oh, right," Dementia grinned.

"I will be leaving soon though. I'm needing to dance again."

"Is it the rage stuff you mentioned last time?" Ennui asked.

"I don't think so. The last few days I keep getting too much energy. If I don't dance it off it keeps building until I want to claw myself apart."


Kali staggered into her flat at 0400. She slipped off her boots inside her entry door and padded up into her flat. In the bathroom she stared at her reflection for a long time. "Stripping down in front of a guy. What were you thinking? And finding guys cute? When did that start?" she asked the silent reflection. No answer came back. "Talking to myself in the mirror again. How special is that? Haven't done that since the Realms."

Danny was still asleep in the pillows when Kali took a quick look. Back in her bedroom she changed into a large T-shirt and fell into bed. Sleep claimed her rapidly for a change.


Sunlight woke Kali two hours later. Everything hurt when she moved. She stifled a moan as she eased out of bed. As she moved the pain slowly decreased to dull, throbbing aches. Downstairs she heard the shower start. She pulled on a thong under her T-shirt and slowly padded down to start coffee. Early morning sunlight filtered into the kitchen and bounced off the hanging pots, throwing sparks of gold everywhere. The ivy shown vivid green in the warm light. Kali stood for a moment and admired the painting like quality of the room before fixing the coffee.

The maker was just finishing when Danny walked in. He was still toweling his hair and making sniffing noises as he followed the fresh scent of coffee. "Ah, a goddess stands before me. She offers up the water of life at this unholy hour of dawn. Yet her feet must be of clay for she neglected to close the drapes and thus deprived me of long morning slumber."

"Cute Danny, real cute," Kali tried to sound mad but she couldn't stop the snicker.

"Might I repay you by preparing an offertory repast?"

"You may." Danny bustled around the kitchen, assembling various items into a large omelet and seasoned potatoes. He brushed off Kali's offers to help. "Go, sit, if you can. I still want you off your feet." Obediently she perched on a stool and watched.

Ten minutes later he placed a small serving in front of her and motioned for her to taste it. "Excellent. Your offering is accepted as a fair trade for the water of life." Kali dished up two large plate fulls and fell upon hers.

"And what are your plans for the day?"

"Temple Heath after this. Anastasia and I have an appointment at noon. Probably dancing at the Devil's Cathouse tonight. And yours?"

"Check your wounds one last time, since I'm here and can. Then restock the med kit on the extraction train and hope for no calls." Danny started water in the sink and reached for the dish soap.

"You can leave those. I'll do them later."

"I want to do them now. I wouldn't feel right leaving you with them."

"You cooked, that means you shouldn't have to clean up."

"I'm glad you feel that way. If this happens again I'll keep it in mind for then," Danny replied as he washed and dried. "You are on the injured list and I want you to stay there while I finish these." He worked on in silence while Kali dutifully remained perched on her stool. "There, now, if I could see your injuries, feet first?"

Kali lifted her feet and presented them to Danny. He looked, then moved closer. Gently he poked at the balls of her right foot. "Does that hurt at all?"

"No, not really. Why? Is something wrong?"

"I'm not sure yet." He turned her foot to get more light on it and pushed against her heel. "How about that?"

"It tickles a little and feels a bit like you're pushing through heavy cloth."

"I've seen some people here adapt in somewhat interesting ways. Looks like you might be one. Take a look at your feet."

Kali pulled her foot up until she could see the underside. Thick darkish pads covered the balls, toe tips, and heel of her foot, making it look like a cross between a human foot and a cat paw. When she poked at the pads it felt cushioned and spongy. "Okay..." She said slowly. "Is this dangerous? Will it spread? I'm not going to morph into a cat or anything, am I? I was getting used to looking like I am now."

"No, you shouldn't. You might need new footwear though," Danny grinned.

Kali stepped down on her feet and did a couple of quick turns and jumps. "Wow, this will make dancing so much easier." She leapt into the air and landed on the balls of her feet. She felt very little jarring in her knees, feet, and ankles. "This is wicked fucking awesome!" She spun in place without any of the sticky, grabbing feel of human skin on floor. "Oh yeah!"

"Before you get too carried away, I'd like to see the others as well." Kali pulled her shirt off. Danny gave the wounds a quick look and said, "These are looking quite good." Kali slipped her shirt back on.

"How does healing work here? In the Realms I healed very slowly and scarred easily. I think my skin didn't like me much."

"That's not all that uncommon of a problem. Here it just depends on the mind of the person. Some heal very rapidly, sometimes within days. Others take a more Realms style length of time. I've heard it's a bit different for the Shadow Walkers, but I don't know for certain about that. You seem to be one of the fast healing people from what I'm seeing with these injuries."

"And the scarring?"

"Time will tell, but right now it looks like you won't have that any more."

Something perverse in Kali's mind remembered his blush as she stripped off her shirt. "So, did you like what you saw?"

Danny turned bright red, thinking of how part of his motive was to get her shirt off again, "I may be a medic but I'm not dead. Ok, I am dead but I'm not dead dead. A beautiful woman still registers." He looked away from her and mumbled, "I'd make a play for you, it's just I think it would be rude right now. But when you're healthy and adaptation reaction is over, I'll be interested until you tell me to stop."

She bit back the half hysteric reply that tried to force its way out. Instead she smiled a tight smile and tried to breath out the tension locking her muscles. "I need to get moving. The energy is building again." She dashed upstairs and hurriedly dressed. "Off to Temple Heath. You can hang around here for a while if you like."

"Yeah, I think I'll finish cleaning up breakfast, then head out."

Outside the morning air felt cool against her flushed skin. She breathed in large breaths to try and still the pounding of her heart. She was calmer by the time she reached Temple Heath. Although she did take ten minutes to run through a few sequences in the yards before venturing to the door and stepping in. She had started toward Bart's office when he waved to her from near Shergar.

"And the legend of Kali continues to grow," he greeted as she walked up.

"It's not my fault, boss."

"And whose would it be then? Lauren came in and was talking to Claire and Erick last night. Seems she needed to decompress before heading home after the mission. Our shadow walking woman doesn't seem to stay in the shadows much."

"Oh gods, not Erick. Shit!"

"Yes, well, he might not be so much of a problem. Lauren did mention you taking Danny home with you. That cooled Erick right down. Then Mark came in looking for Lauren and mentioned her efforts. Erick might be off on another target now."

"Danny helped me home. That's all. He slept downstairs. Nothing Happened."

"Whoa, whoa, I'm not your parents. It wouldn't matter if something had happened."

"But I don't want anything to happen yet. Do you have something you want me to work on?"

Bart stared at her for a moment, then replied, "I'd like you to check out another servo system. She's an EMD SD70M series and she's waiting outside. We don't have room for her inside right now. Let me know if you need a bay with a pit. I'm hoping it's something cab side. Remember, I'm here if you want to talk."

"I know that. Seems like all I do is talk though. I'm not sure if it's helping much."

"It might take some time before you notice the benefit. Now are you going to stand here talking all day or are you going to get to work?"

"Work, yes indeed, right you are." Kali headed to the drawing storage for the necessary drawings.

Claire looked up as she entered. "Welcome back. Sounds like you had an intense time of it yesterday. You doing ok?"

"I'm ok."

"Your medic check you out this morning?"

"It wasn't like that. He just saw me home and crashed on the pillows in the sitting room." Claire seemed to loosen up slightly with the news. "I'm healing well and fairly quickly. Which is good, the slashes on my back and stomach were really painful."

"Fighting naked runs that risk."

"I was not fighting naked. How did that get started?"

"Lauren. You should have seen Erick drool though." Claire laughed. "I thought he was going to lose it right there. Until he heard about your medic. Then he almost choked on his chips. It sounded like you got messed up pretty badly though. You sure you should be here?"

"I'm ok. I can't really stay still anyway, so might as well do something while I'm restless. Speaking of, could you help me find another set of drawings? For an EMD SD70M."

"Sure, all the newer stuff is over in this corner." Claire led the way to the back left section of the room and pulled open a drawer. "In here. The other newer ones are in the rest of these drawers. So, you going to the Cathouse tonight?"

"Planning to, yes."

"Cool."

"Do you know of any dance wear shops in town?" Kali grinned and added, "Fighting naked gets mighty chilly."

Claire laughed in return. "There's one not far from the gothic shop we were in the other day. It's where I got my workout gear for dance classes. They have a wide selection."

"Thanks, catch you later."

Drawings in hand, Kali headed out into the yard. She started to settle onto the floor to slip in to look at the circuitry. Pressure on her back and sides sent shards of pain radiating from her wounds. She stood back up. Sitting in the control chair wasn't quite as bad as long as she didn't lean back.

A quick check of the systems indicated she would have to pull components out. She stood slowly and walked back into the shed. She found Bart in his office. "I'm going to have to wait on the locomotive. I'm a bit too sore to get at all the places I need to check. Sorry about that. If you need it quickly, someone else will need to take a look at it."

"It can wait. You don't need to apologize for getting injured on an extraction. You know you don't have to be here after yesterday. Will you need a bay when you are able to work on it?"

"No, I don't think so. And I know I don't have to be here. I just can't stay still and I was hoping I could do something useful with the excess energy. Guess I can't though." Kali paced around his office. A drawing of a boiler section caught her eye. "Although... Do we have any scrap sheet metal? Say eighth inch thick?"

"I'm sure we do. Why?"

"If I bent it right I could use it to protect my arms and shins the next time out. Who's the best at metal work?"

"Tim, but if you really want precision work, there are a couple of absolute geniuses at Eternal Metal Works. Their shop is in Goth City, just up the line toward Portal Station. Ron Oestrander is the boss man. Or you and Tim can try and bend it up here."

"Anything going up there later? Maybe I'll do that today instead."

"Check at Central Station, but there's almost always traffic between here and there."

"Thanks boss." Kali spent the rest of the morning reviewing the servo systems for the locomotive. She could manage to concentrate as long as she sat forward on a chair, well away from the backrest.

She left a few minutes before noon and arrived at Central Station a few minutes later. A platform agent directed her across platform ten and into a section of large storage areas that had been divided up with temporary walls. Following the largest of the narrow hallways she emerged into an office. Lauren sat behind the only desk going over maps and diagrams. As Kali approached she could see they were the ones from the last mission. "Oh hi Kali. Anastasia is expecting you. I'm just trying to record what happened yesterday for the Hall of Records. They've been trying to keep a history of Eternia going. Through the door to your left, down the hall to the second door on the right."

Kali looked at her hands and kind of waved them a little. "That would be this way," she motioned with her left hand, "and then this way?" she motioned with her right hand. "Sorry, I'm right-left dyslexic."

"You have it."

Kali followed the instructions to another office down the hall. This one was smaller and more crowded than the last. A tiny desk, two chairs, and a book case were wedged into the small room. Scattered everywhere were stacks of plans, maps, and pencil sketches of various places and buildings. Here and there clothing designs in pencil, water colors, and inks were layered over the top. Two torchier lamps struggled to push back the gloom of the enclosed space.

Anastasia squeezed around the end of the desk, grabbed the piles off the guest chair, motioned to Kali to sit, then perched on the edge of her desk. One of the images that flew by looked like one of the tops she had bought when shopping with Claire. "I've seen that before..."

"I design for the goth shop on Elm Hill."

"Wicked! I found some way cool things there the other day."

"I'm glad. I enjoy designing. So, here we are. I have this prepared thing I tell the new comers, but it covers what you already saw. I could tell you to follow instruction better, but that seems like a bad idea after yesterday. I do want to say thank you for sticking to your convictions. I recommend you stay clear of Alisha for a while though. It will take her a while to forgive you, especially since you were right. Do you have any questions now that you've had some time to think over what happened?"

"Not that come to mind. I can't promise I wont go off on my own again."

"Good, because I don't want that promise. Although your fighting style seems rather risky. The entire dive into the thick of them and lay about works as long as they don't have ranged weapons."

"That is a rather good point. Although, if you close fast enough the others in their ranks provide cover."

"True enough. What happens if they bring magic into it? We have started to as you likely noticed."

"Then I'm screwed? Most likely we will field a mix like they will. Lauren seemed to be holding her own quite well. Ennui is another very powerful battle mage. Maybe we could draw on her too?"

"Maybe, when we need another person." Anastasia rose. "Now, let's get you settled in." She led the way farther down the hall to a door on the left. She flipped on a switch and harsh florescent light burst from a wall mounted fixture to light up the cubby of a room. Inside was a tiny desk, chair, and shelf. The walls were of bare plywood and the ceiling was open to the dark vault of the station ceiling high overhead. "All of us get one of these offices, but mostly they get used as a dumping place to keep things in easy grabbing range. You can use it or not at your pleasure. If you want to fancy it up, that's fine too. Your assigned compartment on the train is the same way. In mine I try and keep a spare set of clothes and maybe a weapon or two. Other than that, there is a cache of useful items in the storage area of the common car that everyone can use."

"Damn, I forgot to grab your clothes this morning."

"That's ok. Bring them next time you come down." Anastasia guided Kali back through the maze of small rooms, pointing out various ones and listing off whose it was. "You already know most of the train layout. There is a baggage and equipment car at the rear of the train. That's where the weapons and equipment gets stored. Otherwise, it's mostly what you saw yesterday."

"Wicked, I think I've got it. I have an unrelated question though. I would like to get to Goth City. Whom do I see in the station for scheduling?"

"You could ask anyone on the platforms, or talk to Fred. I think she's usually at the information counter. She has a monitor showing her what Central Dispatch is seeing for local traffic. Are you doing ok? You took a lot of punishment yesterday."

"Surprisingly well actually. Danny checked me out..." she stopped and blushed before amending, "Danny looked over the injuries and they are healing very rapidly and well. As for the bruises and the like, not nearly as painful as I feared."

"Ahh... So anything you'd like to tell me?"

"Gods, what is it with everyone? I'm not interested in Danny that way. I know I could be and it wouldn't be a problem. I'm not ready to go there yet, ok?"

"Ok, ok," Anastasia replied, laughing. "Just one of the common adaptation reactions is the screaming hornies. And one of the most common reactions to a fight like yesterday's is also the screaming hornies."

"Yeah, well, ok.." Kali replied through her bright red face. "I'll be seeing you later." She mumbled as she slipped away. She ran for the nearest women's restroom. Inside she rushed into a stall, snapped the door closed and sank onto the stool. She shook as the emotions of rage, despair, and terror stormed through her. Her skin crawled at the thought of someone touching her. She bit her tongue until it bled to keep from moaning out loud in pain and fear. Tears leaked through her fingers and dropped on her lap as her heart pounded painfully in her chest.

Long minutes passed as she shivered in the small cubicle. Slowly the tears stopped and dried on her face. When the shakes had stopped she pulled her head up out of her hands. Her eyes stared out with a glassy distant stare at her surroundings. She waited until she didn't hear any movement in the room before easing the stall door open. Using paper towels wetted in cold water she cooled her face until the worst of the red puffiness had receded. She stalked from the room with her face set in a neutral mask. Moving swiftly she made her way back to her flat where she collapsed on her bed as a second round of shakes hit.

She slid down into troubled sleep where she ran through dark alleys and narrow caverns, always with hands pulling and grabbing at her. A pushed up section of bricks tripper her, sending her scrambling forward on her hands and knees until dark shapes tackled her and pinned her down. Claws tore and pried at her until her screams yanked her out of sleep. She twisted about in blankets pulled too tight, toppled off the bed, and hit the floor. Twisting and screaming she finally thrashed loose of the blankets. Her breath came in shuddering gasps as she huddled with her back against the bed.

Rather than fading, the terror built energy continued to increase, driving her to her feet. She ran downstairs to her studio, threw CDs into the player and turned it up full. The tinny and thin sound did nothing to help. After a few minutes she snapped it off and hurried back up to her room. She stripped off her boots and the boiler suit, reached into the closet, grabbed the nearest items and pulled them on.

Her bare feet slipped silently down the stairs and out into the night. It wasn't until she stepped onto the cold cobbles that she realized she was barefoot. Shrugging it off, she continued to the Cathouse. She danced off the stairs and into motion. The flashes of thong and thigh, through the slits in her skirt, drew many looks until the watchers saw her face. Then they quickly found other places to look.

When her timing started to slip, as she approached exhaustion, she slipped around behind the bar and ran for the loading platform out back. There she continued to move until she fell. Immediately she sprang back up and continued. Soon she was falling and dragging herself back up. Her fingers tore and bled on the rough brick of the building. Splinters from the wooden decking left tears in her palms. In the far distance the pain almost registered, but it wasn't enough to stop her. Finally she fell and couldn't get back up. Her hands continued to twitch and jerk, trying to force herself up.

Kali floated in a disconnected haze for an unknown time until Ennui's voice started to pull her back. "Kali? Kali, can you hear me? Delirium, run and get Dementia!" A faint warmth registered on her skin where Ennui touched her shoulder.

"What is it? Gods, what happened?" Dementia slid to a halt near Kali.

"I don't know. I came out and found her here. She'd been dancing inside earlier."

"Let's get her up to our rooms." Gently Ennui and Dementia pulled Kali upright. The half carried half walked her up the stairs and settled her on their bed.

"She came in dressed like that? Where are her shoes?" Dementia asked.

"Yes. She came in barefoot."

"Was there any trouble?"

"No. A couple of the usual rowdies were eying her up, but no one did anything to her while she was dancing."

"Not for them," Kali said in a flat, distant, and emotionless voice.

"What's not for them?"

"Not their choice."

"What choice is that?"

"I choose who touches me. No one else has that right." Kali's voice was a little stronger, although it still came from a great distance.

"Of course it's your choice! What gave you any different idea?" Ennui asked.

"Must keep moving. Help me up."

"Kali, you're exhausted. You need to sleep, let your body heal." Dementia reached out and gently touched her shoulder. Shattering images poured into her head. Ruined cities, a bloody, burnt, and screaming child huddled in rubble, dark shapes gliding in the shadows. Her head slammed back into the wall with a crack and her mouth pulled open in a silent scream. Loss, pain, and despair washed over her in waves, followed by a raging stream of chaotic energy, demanding movement. It crawled along her nerves burning itching traceries across her skin. Instinctively Ennui reached for her, stopping when Dementia threw her head back and forth wildly. "Knock down tea, full strength, for Kali, please." Her eyes glazed over as the terrors chasing Kali became hers as well.

In the kitchen Ennui's hands shook as she struggled to prepare the tea. Once the herbs had steeped she dropped ice into it to cool it and, moving as rapidly as she dared, she carried a full cup back to the bed. "Kali, this will help. Please drink it." Kali didn't respond. "Kali," Ennui reached out and touched her hair. Slowly Kali's eyes focused on her. The images released Dementia, slipping away in a receding tide. "Kali, you need to drink this. It will help. I'm going to help you up." Ennui slipped her arm under Kali and helped her to sit up. Dementia placed a shaky hand in the middle of her back to help keep her upright while Ennui held the cup.

"What?"

"It will relax you, stop the images for a while," Dementia whispered softly. Kali's empty eyes swung to her. "It happens to me too. This will help you rest without dreams and visions."

The tea slid down her throat easily with none of the bitter, nasty flavor of the realms medicines. With it came a heavy black warmth. As she faded into darkness she heard a voice in the distance, "Rest now daughter."

Ennui eased Kali back down and met Dementia's haunted eyes over her. "What happened?"

Dementia eased down and wrapped Kali in a tight embrace. "I touched her and everything in her mind crashed into me. I fear for her, Ennui. She is so very troubled. Slide in on the other side of her. She shouldn't be alone." Ennui grabbed a spare blanket from the closet, placed it over the two on the bed, then slid in on the other side of Kali. Dementia reached over and pulled Ennui close to Kali, then reached across to touch her.


Kali woke with the early morning light. Warmth pressed in from two sides. For a moment claustrophobia threatened, then she opened her eyes to see Ennui and Dementia snuggled up against her. A desperate need to pee forced her to move. Two sets of sleepy eyes opened as she tried to slip away. She smiled and slid toward the end of the bed. "Got to pee. I'll be right back." When she returned she started to sit down on the end of the bed until Dementia grabbed her and hauled her back into the middle of them.

"How are you feeling?"

"I'm ok."

"Just ok?" Ennui asked.

"No, actually much better than ok. Thank you both. I'm sorry for being such a pain in the ass."

"Stop, right there. You were not a pain. Don't go adding this to the firestorms in your head." Dementia said.

"What? What did you see?" Kali paled suddenly.

"The wreckage, the screaming girl, and the ash. Don't add this to it. There is no shame in needing help." Dementia replied

"Anything else? Did you see anything else?" panic tinged the edges of Kali's voice.

Dementia pulled Kali down and gently turned her head until she could look in her haunted eyes. "You don't need to fear me. I will not hurt you. That is all I saw."

"I should go," Kali struggled to sit up.

Dementia held her back, "No, you should stay here with friends."

"There are things in my past..."

"You need not tell anything of your time before Eternia. If you wish to, you may, but none expect it. Here you are known by who you are and what you do."

"I feel like I've lost so much, and I don't even know when it happened. One day I looked inside and all I saw was the barren waste. What was I? What happened to me? What was I supposed to be?" Kali drew a shuddering breath and continued, "Most of my life I've felt weird and out of place, and while things here feel so much better, I can't seem to shake the baggage. I survived by staying distant, building masks and shells, and letting no one underneath. Strangers you can shield yourself against. But friends, family, and lovers, they slide in under the radar and carpet bomb your psyche. And now I'm here and the masks are slipping and the old terrors are clawing free. Goddess, I just don't know what to do."

"Kali, it's ok," Dementia said softly, stroking her hair.

"How, how is it ok? I want to explore what this means but all the old shit boils up," She pushed herself toward the edge of the bed.

"Not this time. You might hate us when this is over, but you are staying and talking about this." Dementia grabbed her in a tight hug.

"Why do you dance?" Ennui asked.

"What?"

"Why do you dance?"

"I told you, because I can't stop."

"Would you dance if you didn't have to?"

"No."

"And why not?" Kali stared at Ennui. "Why not?" Ennui asked again.

"Don't want to." Kali dropped her eyes away from Ennui.

"Why not?"

"Leave it alone!"

"No. Why wouldn't you dance if you didn't have to?"

"Alright! Because I'm ugly and clumsy and move like I have a board up my ass..." Kali yelled.

"What is wrong with you?! Have you looked in a mirror lately? Have you heard what anyone says about your dancing? Are you deaf or just fucking stupid?" Kali's head shot up, eyes cold and hard.

"Ennui..." Dementia started.

"No, she's being stupid and she needs to hear this. I don't know who filled her head with crap, but it is not true. Do you hear me, Kali? It Is Not True. I don't know who wanted to destroy you, but do you want them to succeed?"

"Why not? Why not let them succeed? Stupid, selfish, prideful, why shouldn't something like me just end?" Kali snarled back.

"Goddess, is that how you see yourself?" Dementia held her tighter. "That isn't you!"

"You don't know anything about me," Kali spat. "I am all those things and more."

"Bullshit!" Ennui shouted back. She shoved her face right up to Kali's and snarled, "You know less about yourself than your friends. We see you every day. What you do, how, and when. Don't you dare wallow in self despair around me. You want an ass-kicking, fine! Mama y Mama, any time, any where. I'll make you understand if it's the last thing I do!"

"Fuck you! Right here, right now." Kali hissed back.

"Ennui, Kali..." Dementia started.

Two sets of burning eyes swung to regard her and two voices screamed, "What!"

"Fine, just fine," she muttered, backing away slowly. They sprang from the bed and circled each other like two stalking cats. Just before they pounced Dementia leapt between them. "Gods damn it all! Stop acting like men."

""Men?" two voices screeched.

"Yes, men, beating your chests and getting ready to pound on each other. Stop this before you both get hurt. Kali, you don't have the truth of yourself. No one does, not without all sorts of mystic mumbo jumbo, and even that rarely works." She slowly walked toward Kali, hands open and spread. Kali stood still, shaking and panting, but some of the rage had bled out of her eyes. Gently Dementia cupped her face, "You deserve so much more than you believe. If you can't think well of yourself, let us do it for you and listen to what your friends say. It is more objective than what you cook up inside your head. Religions have it wrong when they say what's in your heart is most important. What you do in the world defines you and matters the most. You have done many good things and you need to accept that it makes you good as well."

Kali backed away, her head shaking from side to side violently. "No, no, can't be good. Don't want to be good. Good means responsibility, expectations, being judged, playing by someone else's rules. Fuck that!" She continued backing away until she hit the wall. There she stayed, hands raised claw-like in front of her.

"Kali, it's not that way here. You belong. No one will take that from you. No one will judge you unworthy of it."

"I just want to belong. Why can't I ever feel like I belong?" Kali wailed as she slid down the wall, curled in on herself, and shuddered with long wracking sobs.

Ennui slid down beside Kali and wrapped her arms around her. "You belong here in Eternia." Dementia sat down on the other side of Kali and added her arms to the tangle.

"I just feel so empty and scared. I had dreams once. Insane, crazy dreams, impossible dreams, but they kept me alive and...operational...through my teens and early adulthood. One day I "woke up" and realized they could never happen. Ever since then I've just been empty, staggering through life because I was either too stubborn or too scared to die. I don't even know which, probably scared, that seems to be me, scared of everything and everyone. Once I leave here I'll freak because you know too much about me now. You've seen it, the shattered wastes," Kali stared at Dementia through distant eyes.

"Let this place give you a dream back. This would be 'impossible' from a Realms perspective, wouldn't it," Dementia replied. "Try not to fear your friends. Why would we want to destroy you?"

"Why would my parents want to? Yet they were always telling me I was nothing special, that anyone could do what I do, that my ego was too large."

"Who knows, but they aren't here. You are free of them. And your ego isn't large enough from what I've seen."

"I need to go. Bart'll be waiting."

"Not today. Today you stay here with your friends and we show you we aren't going to hurt you. Ennui will have someone tell Bart the last rescue caught up with you."

For a few more minutes Kali was able to sit there, then her hands started to rub at her arms and head. Soon she pushed herself up and began to pace jerkily around the room. "It begins again," she moaned.

"You can use the dance floor if you want. Turn on the amps on the lighting platform, shove some CDs into the changer and bring up the first fader on the sound board. That should get music for you. Are you going to want food?" Ennui asked.

"Thanks. Maybe food later, but not now." She practically ran from the room.

"Go with her, see if you can stop her before she collapses again. I'll bring you some food and coffee soon," Dementia told Ennui. Kali was already in motion when Ennui arrived. She stood quietly in the shadows observing. Slowly a devious plan formed in her mind. She was grinning to herself when Dementia slipped in behind her and wrapped her arms around her. "Hey love, your coffee and food are on the bar. How's she doing?"

Ennui turned so she could speak into Dementia's ear over the pounding music, "Showing no signs of slowing down. I have something I'd like to try later." Dementia quirked her eyebrows. "If you could get her out of here just before band practice today, then arrange to bring her back when we are practicing. I want to see how she reacts to our stuff."

"That's not all, is it?"

"No, but I want to see what happens before I say any more."

"Sure, I'll try."

Several hours later Kali slowed to a stop and approached Dementia on shaky legs. By the time she reached the bar a large glass of water was waiting. Kali smiled and asked, "Might I raid the kitchen for food?"

"You could, or we could go grab some elsewhere."

"I did want to go back to the goth shop and the dance wear shop on Elm Hill anyway. Is Ennui going to join us?"

"She has a few things she needs to do here." Dementia replied as she led the way out of the club. The sky was dark and heavy with a damp grey fog woven between the buildings. "How are you doing?"

"Fine."

"Are you sure?"

"What do you want me to say? Everything has changed and I still don't know how to cope? My head is still full of shit and I don't know if it will ever get better? Why should I burden those around me with my trivial issues? I've already been hijacking your time, Ennui's time, and Bart's time. At this rate I'll be stopping people in the streets next."

"Ennui's right, you need to see yourself for what you really are."

"I do."

"Then tell me something you like about yourself."

"What?"

"Tell me something you like about yourself. It's a simple enough request."

Kali walked in silence for many steps before answering, "I'm not fat anymore."

"And?"

"And what?"

"And what else do you like?"

"This is ridiculous!"

"No, it's not. You see your flaws in sharp, over-examined detail, but you don't have a clue about your good points. While you are thrashing around in your head you might consider that you dance better than most professionals and you don't have the ego problems they do. You are brave and strong enough to fight for your friends and you have the courage to talk to people about yourself, something many can't do at all. You care about the people around you, even though you don't want to believe it." She grabbed Kali's arm as Kali turned. "Not this time."

"Do you think you can really stop me?" Kali asked in an icy tone.

"Only if part of you wants to stop running." Dementia said, staring straight back into Kali's stormy eyes. "What happened to you?"

"I don't know! I don't remember being raped, beaten mercilessly, or seriously messed with like some of my friends. Yet my first reaction to any contact is threat assessment, fear, and distancing. The closer someone gets the more I fear them."

"And why is that wrong? Things can be dangerous."

"I want to understand how some people can smile at strangers, can say hello without their insides twisting. How can they be friendly knowing how anybody can be a hostile?"

"They believe the world isn't always hostile. It's not always easy, but it can be done. You could do it too if you really want to."

Kali slowed as they entered Elm Hill. "Look, could we grab coffee and find a quiet place for a few minutes before I go shopping?"

"Ok, but I thought you were hungry too?"

"I was, but I'm not any more. Maybe later."

Dementia led the way to the coffee shop she liked near the Goth Shop. The trees and plants looked slightly wilted under the weight of the fog. The outside tables were empty but sounds of conversations and the hiss of an espresso machine came from within. Dementia led the way to the counter and ordered. Kali started to but changed her mind when nerves tightened her stomach. She idly scanned the room while Dementia waited, noticing the small brick enclosed patio out the back of the shop. Kali headed that way once Dementia had her order. Kali settled into a chair behind the farthest table with the best view of the door. Water dripped slowly from the ivy and trees overhead and onto her head and shoulders, drawing a small twitch from her, but not enough for her to move. Once Dementia was settled in facing her she began, "I was going to tell you about before..."

"You don't have to..."

"I do. It is why I am so...clueless, i guess, about so much," Kali stopped as fear clenched her heart. "I wasn't...I wasn't...." she stopped as black spots danced in front of her eyes and dizziness almost spun her from the chair. For long moments she struggled to control the panic and catch a breath.

"Kali, it's ok, you don't have to say..."

"I was born male, I didn't want to be, and I hated every part of it, but that's how everyone tried to raise me," Kali stopped again as her nerve failed once more.

"Wow, that's more change than most of us, no wonder your head's a mess!"

"Instant change with no understanding of what to do with the changes. Everything is so different and not and...and..." The shakes hit her hard, almost flinging her from the chair. She dropped her head into her hands and tried to ride it out.

Dementia leaned over and pulled Kali tight to her, stroking her hair softly, "Hey, easy, easy, it's ok. I mean it's a shock, but it's ok. I was afraid you were going to say you were a child molester or something. I would never have guessed, you seem just like every other woman I've ever known, maybe a bit stronger and more self-possessed, but that's it. So, do you want to talk about it? I'd like to listen if you do..." Kali remained silent and shaking in her arms. "Hey, hey, it's ok. Now you can be who you want to be." Slowly Kali wrapped her arms around Dementia.

"I don't want this to be an 'oh, poor pitiful me' session. I fucking hate talking about this. My past is nobody's business but I need someone to understand, someone I can ask for help. Fuck, fuck, fuck!" Tears leaked from her eyes and dripped onto Dementia's shoulder. "I don't want to be a freak, but I'm still a freak, even here, even now, just a goddamned freak." She clung to Dementia as shudders wracked her.

"Look, I've got a clue for you, everyone is a freak. Normal's just a way to enforce control. I'm a freak, I get 'visions from the devil', at least that's what I was told. Ennui was a circus girl. To the rest of her world she was an outsider, a freak, if you will."

"I'm sorry." Kali said after a while as she started to pull away.

"No. How many times do I have to tell you? You don't have to run from me." Dementia said as she tightened her grip. "This isn't a pitiful Kali session. You want me to understand you, that is always a good thing. We can stay here or go, but I am serious, you shouldn't be alone today." Dementia slowly released Kali as she settled down.

"Stay, I guess." Kali stared into space for a very long time. "I don't know how to talk about it. It consumes your every thought, how wrong you feel in any gender charged situation, how uncomfortable in your own skin, how freaky you must be. Watching the kids around you change the way you want to and seeing yourself change some other way. Now that's all over, but I'm still the freak in my head, pounded by the fucked up gender roles everyone tried to teach me as I was growing up."

"What do you mean?"

"When we'd play house as little kids I never wanted to be the mommy or the daddy. By my second year in school I knew I never wanted children. It seemed the ultimate cruelty to bring one into the world and subject them to the others. I hated having to be either the subservient 'wife' or the macho, overbearing 'husband'. I wanted to be the mad scientist in the empty castle on the hill, the shadow walker, or the starship captain alone in the void. I wanted to run screaming from normal life, step out of the bullshit. And yet I tried to settle down but it didn't really work. Then I met others with my condition and saw how badly it can fuck you up. Somehow I got off easy. I wasn't completely insane. I could function and make some friends and get by in the world. But I still never wanted to be there. This, Death City, is a fantasy, but how do I adapt? I still have all the old responses, distrust, a desire to remain distant, to keep the hurts away...And now I'm fucking rambling about shit that shouldn't even concern me any more."

"No one automatically adapts to sudden change. You are what you want, but you need to give yourself time to catch up. You should ask Bart about sudden changes. He would be happy to tell you about his. It's not the same as yours, but it left him confused and uncertain for a long time."

"But I'd have to tell him about this."

"You wouldn't. It's accepted fact that everyone here has likely had at least one massive change to adapt to. It's one of the reasons for adaptation reaction in general."

"And about confusion..." Kali slowed to a stop, face flaming. Dementia waited, afraid any words would stop Kali from continuing. "I, uh, I have never had a....period," the last word was spoken so softly Dementia almost didn't catch it.

"It's different for everyone, it's a bit of a mess, passing the blood and all, but not a really big deal. Keep some napkins or something on hand and you will be fine. If you had girlfriends, you probably know more about this than you think already."

"Will it hurt?"

"Only if you get cramps. Otherwise, not really. I've known a few people who say they could feel the blood moving, but I'm not one of them. Mostly, it's just another thing in life to get used to." Kali looked down at the ground. "Was there something else you wanted to ask?"

"When I came here, I was only interested in women. Now I'm finding some boys cute too..."

"You've changed. Wouldn't it make sense that who you are attracted to might also change? You're not very comfortable with your sexuality, are you?" Kali continued to stare at the ground and shook her head. "Because of the other thing?"

"Maybe somewhat, but it's always been weird for me for other reasons as well. Casual sex seemed too risky, both from emotional issues and disease or pregnancy. Sex with a close partner always felt difficult, sort of forced and kind of like I wasn't respecting them. I came from a home life that was way too religious and lacking in any sort of close emotional contact. By my family's definitions, just about everything in life was wrong or sinful. When I hit puberty they handed me a book and said it would answer my questions. To their credit, it did, but it was very impersonal and distant. I think my parents would have been happier if my sister and I had been robots, only active when ordered to do something."

"Sounds pretty bad, but you did survive it. That says a lot. I'm not totally comfortable with sex either. About the only person I know who is would be Ennui. She loves everything about it and has helped me loosen up a lot. I'd suggest you talk to her if you want some ideas on how to cope." Kali shrugged nervously and Dementia dropped what she had been about to say.

The silence stretched out for long minutes. Finally Dementia asked, "Would you mind if I asked you something?" When Kali nodded ok she continued, "If it wasn't about the gender roles, why did you feel the need to change?"

"It was never about the fucked up social roles, or even about clothes, like it seems to be for so many of my kind. It was about basic body image. I hated the boy bits and the boy chemistry, the grindy testosterone driven rage and despair, and the ugly chunk of meat between my legs. One of my earliest memories is of looking down and seeing that meat hanging there and wishing it would go away. I felt ugly and then my parents gave me the boy hair cut of the time, hair shaved to half and inch or less all over my head, which intensified the ugliness. I hated the social roles I saw growing up and never wanted either of them. People should be able to wear what they want, do what they want, be who they want without some artificial social construct telling them it's wrong. I spent my first adolescence in Alaska. There were plenty of examples of strong women for role models so I never felt the need to be anything other than who I was." Kali stared into the distance and tried to bring her breathing back under control. "Why does it have to be such a loaded thing, to just be? It matters who you sleep with, it matters what's in your crotch. Why is it always such a big deal to people? Don't they have enough of their own shit to keep them occupied?"

"It's always easier to worry about someone else. Takes the attention away from themselves. Lets them feel better about what they are. It does suck though," Dementia replied. "In a perfect world, what would you want?"

"To know what it's like to grow up coherent, mind and body in agreement. To have experienced normal puberty and dating and all the rest."

"Think about the coherent people you've known, how are they? Are they any less confused, hurt, messed up, than you? Maybe it would have been better in some ways, but I don't think it would have been as different as you want to believe. Your path gave you strength and courage and an understanding that few ever reach. Would you truly want to give that up?" She took in Kali's non-believing stare. "Whatever things were like where you came from you can put it behind you here. No one will ever know anything that you don't tell them. That's the rule from the Lady, even if your closest friend from the Realms arrived tomorrow, they wouldn't be able to spill anything but their own past. It's weird and crazy but it works. You can reveal this about yourself or let it slide away as you choose. Still, it is part of what has made you who you are. Without it you might not have come here and that would have been tragic for those you have helped and a diminishing of those of us who are your friends. Try to think about that when next you spiral into that head of yours."

"Bart accuses me of thinking too much."

"And he would be right about that. Life suffers from too much analysis. Dance instead. You obviously love it and the rest of us appreciate the beauty."

"It's not that easy..."

"No, it's not. You can let your scars and demons consume you or you can own them and live anyway. Those are the only choices. Nothing magically removes them, not even this place."

"So comforting..."

"You want me to lie to you too? I think too many have done that in your past already."

"No, you're right. I just want a reboot, I want to edit the crap out of my head, from twisted religion, to self loathing, to the belief I am worthless. I just want it to stop!"

"Yeah, you, me, Ennui, everyone I know... We all wish it were that easy. Since it isn't we support each other as best we can."

"Would you..."

"Of course, silly. You should know that by now. You doing better?" She watched Kali nod. "You might consider telling Ennui as well. It would make it easier when you want to ask for help."

"Yeah, I guess," Kali replied reluctantly. "I just don't want to end up defined as Kali the trans person. I hated that in the Realms."

"I wouldn't worry about that. You are already defined as Kali the Dancer and Kali the Warrior Woman. Although this explains what was confusing Claire so much the other day. She says you went shopping and freaked out on her."

"I always freak out shopping. Too many choices and my brain freezes. It can be shopping for clothes, food, even deciding where to go out to eat."

"That wasn't what freaked her, it was the never dressing to impress. I guess this explains that too, doesn't it?"

"If you've never liked the way you look, the thought of calling attention to yourself is really creepy, if it occurs to you at all. Dressing up and, by extension, dressing to impress, always felt like more of a reinforcement of the social rules rather than something to do for fun. Plus, relationships are complicated enough when there aren't odd body parts getting in the way. I dreaded being hit on, finding I liked it, and then having to figure out how to explain. Better to avoid the dangers of that situation entirely. I'm not sure how I feel about it here."

"You won't have to worry about it."

"Why not?" Kali asked. "Please tell me."

"I don't mean this to be hurtful. You are very aware of when people are watching you and you respond with a look that is distant, empty, and a bit predatory. It certainly wouldn't encourage anyone with even a bit of perception. Only the totally clueless would go any further."

Kali rose, "I need to get going. Soon I'll have to dance again and I really need to get a few things before then."

"I wish you wouldn't look at it as have to dance again. You make it sound so bad."

"Alright, I will be dancing again soon, that better?" Kali answered as she headed for the door.

"Yes, and I want you to think that way every time the need hits. Adaptation reaction won't last forever and I selfishly don't want you to stop dancing when it ends."

"Fine," Kali replied as she opened the door to the Goth Shop.

"Bare foot today? Didn't like the boots?" The woman behind the counter called.

"No, the boots are wicked awesome, it's just my feet need to go bare foot often or they eat themselves. I need a few more items, so, I'm back again!"

Kali crossed to the rack of camouflage cargo pants. She reached for her old size, then reconsidered and grabbed several to try. Once she found the right new size she grabbed several pairs, stopped and grabbed a variety of thongs, waved at the woman behind the counter, and headed for the door.

"You actually like thongs?" Dementia asked when they were outside.

"Yeah, they don't crawl, bunch up, or chafe when I'm dancing."

"Okayyyy. You don't mind the permanent wedgie feeling of them?" Dementia asked.

"No, not really," Kali answered.

Kali pulled open the door to the dance shop Claire had mentioned. It was a small shop with a display of toe-shoes, a sampling of basic dance wear displayed on the walls, and several small tables and bins holding sealed packages. She crossed to the leotards and started looking. After a few moments she turned away and walked to the counter. "Uhm, I've just gone through the Eternia form change and I'm not sure what size I am anymore. Can I open a couple packages and try those on?" Kali pointed back toward the leotards.

"You can, or I can take a few quick measurements for you. That way you'll know for other clothes as well."

"Uh, ok, that would be nice..." Kali blushed deeper as the woman ran a tape around her in various different directions, scribbling numbers on a pad after each time.

"There, looks like medium if you like them a little tight or large if you like them just a bit loose. Go try a couple on if you want."

Kali grabbed a couple and headed for the dressing rooms. A few minutes later she emerged, wearing camo pants and one of the leotards. She grabbed a couple more and started to leave.

"Hey, you want your measurements?" The woman called from the desk. Kali returned and took the offered paper. "You look familiar, do you hang out at the Devil's Cathouse?"

"Sometimes."

"Was that you dancing last night? That was so cool! Do you take students?"

"What?"

"Lots of pros take on a few students for cash, at least they did in the Realm I'm from. I would like you to teach me if you're taking students."

"Students? Teach? I didn't even know how to dance before I came here. I wouldn't know how to teach, I'm sorry."

"Oh, I'm sorry, I guess I thought...It's ok, just if you ever do, please let me know. I'd love to have you teach me your style."

"Uh, ok, right, um thanks for the measurements, and all..." Kali hurried out the door before spinning to Dementia. "That was really weird."

"No one ever ask you to show them anything before?"

"Not a total stranger."

"I tried to tell you how good you are. Does that help convince you?"

"I guess so."


At the Devil's Cathouse

Throbbing dark rhythms met them as they walked back into the Cathouse. Kali dashed down the stairs, threw her bags toward the bar, and launched into motion. She didn't notice the lights were up, only the music mattered.

On stage Ennui smiled broadly and motioned to the rest of the band. Instantly the music stopped. "That seems good. Maybe we should go over the opening once more. Claire, you ready on lights?" When the stage lights bumped quickly the lead guitarist set her instrument in a stand and climbed on the gurney at the back of the stage. Ennui, and two others walked back to it and pushed it to the center of the stage. Ennui crossed to her bass while the others moved to drums and keyboards. The drummer smashed a mallet into a huge gong. The lights flashed once. The drummer slammed the gong again and the lights flashed once again. The drummer began a slow heartbeat rhythm and the keys came in with a low, haunting melody. Kali began mouthing words without even noticing as she danced. The gong crashed again. Suddenly the keys gave forth a shriek and the figure on the bed twitched. Kali raised her arms aloft and screamed, "Life, give my lover life!"

The band faltered for a moment and Kali dropped her arms as she realized she had spoken. "Kali, what did you say?" Ennui called from the stage.

"No.. nothing...I'm sorry..."

"Really, we'd like to know. It sounded like it would fit the music. Please."

"I, I really don't remember. I was dancing and then I heard someone shouting, then you called to me."

"Claire, would you get Kali a headset. Kali, would you let Claire record what you say?"

"I'd rather not."

"You won't have to listen to it. It would let us hear what you said." Claire held up a headset microphone.

"Well...ok...but I probably won't even remember what I said before. And remember, you promised, I don't have to listen to it, ever!" Kali reluctantly agreed as she took the offered mic. She slipped it on and waited for the opening to begin again. This time through the band didn't stop when Kali shouted. They kept going to the end of the first number.

Ennui motioned for playback and stood listening to Kali's track. "Wow, listen to this, this is perfect! Claire, send it to the rest of the band, ok?"

Kali jerked rigid as her voice sounded in her ears. She opened her mouth to scream, then closed it as she listened to a low alto voice with dark over tones and a hint of an eastern European accent. Her words were haunting and powerful, telling of a dead lover and a desire to bring her back to life.

"Kali, that's great! May we use it? It so fits the idea for the opening. Bella, you could add some more haunting keyboard and we could sing over it."

"I think Kali should sing it. It needs a darker voice." Claire said through the headphones.

"I don't think Kali should sing it," Kali replied.

"You should, and you should dance with the band, at least for the first night back. It would so totally rock the house and be a great way for the band to come back."

"Come back? What do you mean?"

"The rescue where we met? We lost one of the band on that mission. When we next play it will be the first time since then." Ennui answered.

"Oh, I'm sorry, I didn't know. Claire, I'm no performer, I don't think I could do it."

"Sure you could. With the headset mic you could be anywhere, even in with the rest of the dancers."

"Although, it would be really cool to have you up on stage with us," Ennui countered. "I remember several bands from the realms that had stage dancers. You certainly have the moves."

"No, no, I think I like Claire's idea better," Kali replied, face burning. "I'm not a performance dancer."

"Bullshit," the drummer countered. "You're as good as the best I've seen."

"Kali, this is Audrey, Nightshade on stage," Ennui introduced the drummer. "And this is Beth, Belladonna on stage, our keyboardist, and Maggie, Nausea on stage, our lead guitarist and the other vocalist."

"You should at least give it a try. Rehearse with us a few times and see how it feels. I think you'd be great!" Maggie added.

"And people are watching you on the dance floor anyway. Remember the dance shop clerk," Dementia called from the bar.

The itching burn of energy began to crawl along Kali's nerves again. "Ok, I'll practice a bit, just let's get started again." Ennui flashed her a questioning look. At Kali's nod she motioned to begin. They ran through the opening several times, each time Kali was a little less tentative with her vocals.

After the fourth run-through Kali said, "This seems good, but we could make it a lot more theatrical."

"Oh?" Ennui asked.

"Image this for example. Start with a dark stage with a single spotlight on the back entry. A doctor looking character pushes a table into the center of the stage, followed by the usual hunchback assistant. The doctor begins a pantomime of stitching together a body from various parts. Once in a while asking the assistant for another body or a part. This is where my current vocals go, as well as some nice haunting, creepy keyboards. At the end of it the doctor and assistant attach the table to a lift and haul it up to the roof. There the fake body gets switched with Maggie and we use the lightning and thunder effects. Once the table is lowered Maggie rises and you launch into the second half of the lyrics, something about a dead girl living again."

"Hmm, might work," Maggie commented. "Although we'd have to get mods made to the club."

"Not a problem," Dementia called from the bar. "The back sections are above here, shouldn't take much to pull more floor and the lift we can get from the sorting center. Probably be done middle of next week. You still planning for next friday as your new debut?"

"I think so. Kali, can you have the rest of the lyrics by early next week?"

"Rest of what lyrics?"

"To Dead Girl Living of course. It's your concept, it should be your song."

"Wait a minute, I'm not even a musician."

"You are now, unless you want out. You should give it a try though. Just think poetry to music, that helps me." Beth replied.

"Uh, right. Could you guys play some more? I really ne...want to dance some more." Kali headed for the stairs down from the stage.

"Where are you going?"

"Back to the dance floor, unless you are running the opening again."

"If your going to be the stage dancer you should get used to the stage."

"Oh, right, ok."

Several hours later Dementia called, "Club opens in an hour. You might want to pack it up."

Once the gear was moved off the stage Kali headed to the bar to pick up her clothes. "Kali, you want to stay for dinner? It'll be bar food but I expect you'd be coming back anyway, so this will be easier." Dementia offered.

"True. I'll stay, thanks."

Kali finally staggered home long after midnight. She reached for the doorknob and only vaguely registered the note taped to it. Half way up the stairs it registered enough for her to go back and read it. "Kali, I stopped by to see how you are doing. No one has seen you today and I was wondering. I'm going to wait a while in case you come in late. I'm on the pillows in the living area. If I'm asleep, see you in the morning, I hope. Danny."

Kali slipped into the living area and looked down. Danny was curled up in the pillows, peaceful in sleep. Kali smiled, grabbed a spare blanket from her room and draped it over him. He stirred in his sleep, pulled it up under his chin, and settled back down. Upstairs Kali fell into bed and slipped into sleep.


Kali woke cross-wise on the bed with vague memories of tormented sleep. "Still not sleeping?" Danny asked as she stumbled down the stairs.

"Not very well."

"Are you doing ok otherwise?"

"Yeah, why do you ask?"

"You weren't around yesterday and Anastasia was fairly certain she'd freaked you out the day before. She said you left looking really strange, either very angry or very hurt, she wasn't sure."

"It wasn't really anything."

"Kali..."

"Look, this is all just so new, the fighting, the healing, the magic, trains to different worlds. It catches up to me sometimes, just how much everything changed in the last couple of weeks."

"About that healing..." Kali pointed at her legs. "Damn, these look like you've had them a week or more. Guess that answers your question. Is there any pain, swelling, or discoloration on any of the others?"

Kali shook her head. "No. You know another thing I love about this place? I can go to the Cathouse, stay until I'm almost deaf, and my ears are fully healed by morning. And the best thing of all, I can breathe clearly on a daily basis."

"What do you mean about the breathing? Were you asthmatic before?"

"I think I might have been. Most mornings I would end up in at least one major coughing fit. Cold weather, car exhaust, most perfumes and cleaning products would prompt the same reactions."

"Sounds asthmatic to me. Glad that's gone for you as well. So, you want food? I'm cooking again."

"You don't have to cook this time. I didn't think I had any food after the last time."

"You didn't. I went to the market on my way over last night, and it's no problem, I like to cook. Let me treat you again. That way I can be sure you're eating enough."

"I'm eating fine."

"You do realize you aren't sleeping well and are dancing and exercising more than most."

"I don't want to start eating too much and get fat like I was in the realms."

"If you don't get enough food your body will start to eat itself and it will effect your dancing. I'd appreciate it if you kept track of your weight for a while, until you know you are eating enough."

"Well, ok. I am a little bit hungry," Kali sat and watched Danny for a few minutes before finally asking, "Why all this interest in me?"

"I consider you a friend and I take care of my friends." He set a large section of cheese, mushroom, and sausage omelet in front of her.

"We don't even know each other."

"I've seen you naked, fixed you up, and helped you home. That should count for something."

"I guess," she responded slowly. "But lots of people have seen me almost naked of late."

"That's true. Doesn't stop me from wanting you for a friend."

"If you say so," Kali launched into her food.

"Would you mind if I asked you something?" Danny asked a few minutes later.

"If I do, I won't answer," Kali smiled to take the sting from the words.

"I've always wanted to ask women why they shave their pubes."

"Wow, let's get personal, but I'll answer it if you answer why do men shave their faces?"

Danny laughed, "Ok, I shave because my beard comes in ragged and itches like a mad fiend. Shaving is just easier."

"Fair enough. I shave because I like the look. Although," Kali's eyes danced with mischief in her bright red face, "I'm thinking it looks a little plain down there. Maybe I should spice it up with piercings or tattoos."

She openly grinned at Danny's wince. "Ouch! It looks very fine down there, really."

"And you are a connoisseur? How many have you seen?" She shot back, trying to ignore the surge of interest her body felt at his admiration.

Danny blushed bright red, "Enough. I am a medical professional after all."

"And how do I stack up?" Panic flickered across her face as she realized she actually asked what she was thinking. "Oh gods, I didn't just ask that, forget I asked that. Don't answer that!" She leapt up and dashed from the room. Up stairs she threw on a boiler suit and boots. Her face was still bright red as she hurried for the door out.

"You are beautiful," Danny murmured under his breath as he sat back, trying to sort through the strange signals Kali had been sending. "You are one strange woman, Kali," he thought while starting on the dishes.

Nervous energy kept Kali moving at an almost run to Temple Heath. Once there she spent twenty minutes in the yard trying to dance off enough of it to concentrate on the day ahead. She grabbed the plans for the servo system she had tried to work on previously and headed out to try again. The conversation with Danny kept popping into her thoughts the instant her attention wandered. Over and over she analysed it, but couldn't figure out why she had asked that last question.

After a fruitless hour she stalked into the shop, threw the plans on her bench, and found Bart. "I'm sorry, I won't be able to work on that servo today either." She pushed shaking hands through her hair and tried to find something else to say. Energy boiled off her in waves, making Bart start to shift in sympathetic nervousness. "I'm headed to Goth City. You need anything taken up or brought back?"

"No, thanks for asking. Are you ok?"

"Yeah." Her look discouraged any more questions.

"Ok, see you later then."

She ran for the station, arriving out of breath and almost calm. She hurried through the main section of the station and hunted around through the cavernous building until she found the information kiosk. Seated inside was a librarian looking woman leaning back with a large book propped up on her lap. "Fred?"

"Yes?" She looked up from a large book. "Do I know you?"

"No. Anastasia told me to come find you. I was wanting to know about any train scheduled to the area near Eternal Metal Works. I'm Kali by the way."

"Kali? The Kali? I expected you to look larger somehow."

"The Kali?"

"Yeah, the Kali of extraction team fame. I expected you to be more fearsome or something."

Kali rolled her eyes. "Guilty as charged. Although I don't feel very fearsome."

"Riiight. Not the way I've heard it told. Anyway..." Fred looked down and typed a few keys. "I show a small freight leaving in ten minutes from platform 5. If you hurry you can make it." She hit a few more keys. "Give the driver this cab permit and you can ride the jump seat."

"Wicked, thanks! Uh, which way?"

Fred pointed down the massive entry hall and to the left. Kali dashed off in the indicated direction. She slid to a brief stop when she saw the sign for platform 5. She arrived beside the locomotive just as the driver was finishing a walk around. "Hi,"

"Hi. Kali isn't it? I thought you'd be, you know, larger, more muscular, somehow."

"How do you know me?"

"How many curly red haired women have you seen wearing a boiler suit wandering around Death City? I figured it was a good guess."

"Yeah, guess so. Fred gave me this cab permit. I'm trying to get to Eternal Metal Works."

"No trouble, come with me. I've got some stuff to drop there as well." He smiled and waved her into the cab. "Take the jump seat over there. I'm Alex." He concentrated for a few minutes getting the train cleared and in motion out of the station. "It's about fifteen minutes to the Goth City switches, then another ten to the metal works. I'm afraid I'm not really the talkative sort. Hope you don't get too bored."

"I'm good. Got a lot on my mind anyway." Kali settled back and tried not to let her mind drift toward Danny and the morning.

"Guess extractions might do that to a person. You've got a lot more courage than I do. I admire that." Kali's eyes popped open. "I don't think I could go out on one of those. How do you do it?"

"Maybe I'm an excitement junky. I don't know."

"Seems pretty heroic to me."

Kali stared at him from eyes gone cold and hard. "Look, I'm no hero. I'm just a screwed up girl trying to figure out who she is. Don't try to make me something I'm not." She turned and stared out the window.

"A hero is someone who is in the wrong place at the wrong time and makes the best choices to get people back from it. I didn't mean to upset you. Others see you very differently than you see yourself."

"Yeah, and they'd be wrong."

"Would they be? I wonder..." Alex watched as she stared stiffly out the window. "Maybe you're the one who's wrong. Or, maybe, in the end, it doesn't matter at all who is right or wrong, just that you were there." The rest of the trip passed in silence as his words seeped into Kali's thoughts.

Twenty minutes later they pulled between two towering brick buildings and into a large switch yard sourrounded by more large brick buildings. Dust grimed windows and sagging, closed doors marked many of them. Only three had open doors, lights, and sounds of activity. Alex motioned to the center building. "Come on, I'll introduce you to Ron." He swung down from the cab and started toward the doors. Kali hurried to follow.

Inside sounds of hammering, the hiss of welders, and the smell of hot metal washed over her. Alex turned to the nearest person and asked, "Ron around?"

"In the office."

Alex turned left and started up a steep stairway. It wound around the inside of the building to a set of rooms overlooking the main floor. "Ron, this is Kali."

"Kali, welcome. Bart told me to expect you. What can we do for you?" Sparkling devilish green eyes glinted in a roundish, sun burned face. What hair he had left was bone white.

"I need some sheet steel cut and bent. Bart recommended your team."

"We can do that. Alex, you here with the steel?"

"Yup. If we could get that unloaded I'll be on my way."

"Terry can get you set. He's back with the milling machines right now."

"Great Ron. See you around, Kali."

"Thanks for everything," Kali added.

"I'm going to introduce you to Rainy. She handles model making and fabrication planning. She'll get you what you need." Ron rose and led the way back downstairs. He crossed the main floor and entered a smaller section of benches, wood and clay working tools, and partially finished models of odd mechanical pieces. "Rainy, you back here?"

"Hey boss," A head of bright red hair poked out of a side room, followed by a black clad woman. "What's up?" She was just a bit shorter than Kali and solid, muscular, with a round face and a warm smile. "Kali, isn't it? I love your tattoo! Did you design it?"

"Hi. Did we meet? I'm afraid I don't remember..."

"A couple of days ago, on Farlirish. I was in that cluster of people you dodged through. What do you need?"

"I was hoping to get forearm and shin guards bent out of some sheet steel. Bart sent me over here."

"Good choice on his part. Anything you needed boss? Otherwise I can get Kali's project done in a couple of hours." Ron shook his head and headed back for the office. "We can do that. What did you have in mind?"

"I was thinking eighth inch sheet metal curved to fit around and held on with some type of velcro straps."

"It's possible, however, anything solid enough to be effective will be heavy. From what I've heard of how you fight, it might hurt more than help. And it would be something that could get grabbed or hooked with claws. Here, let me show you what you want would weigh." Rainy pulled Kali into one of the back storage areas and over to a bin of smaller pieces of metal. She grabbed one and put it in Kali's hand. "This is about the size you would need."

Kali lifted it, moved it in the motions she would use, then handed it back. "It seemed like a good idea, but it would be too heavy. Sorry to have bothered you."

"No bother at all. Would you pass on my thanks to the rest of you team for saving our asses? I didn't get a chance to talk to Anastasia."

"Of course. Guess I should find a train back. Where would I find a station?"

"We're not very busy. I can show you, on one condition."

"What?"

"Tell me about the real Kali, the legend is already confusing."

"Legend? What the fuck?"

Several heads came up at Kali's outburst. Then someone pointed and Kali just heard, "That's her."

"Come on, the sub-train connection is in the office building. We can talk along the way." Rainy practically dragged Kali out of the building. "Look, more and more people are afraid to go out because of the interference by the proxy gods and their minions. At first it was just a minor darkling or two trying a few scare tactics. Now real damage is being done to people and equipment. And with the death of Le Mort, the killings have started as well. You're the first one to stand up and kick ass. Anastasia and her people are good defenders, but it will take more than that to keep us safe."

"But Sammi and Jemima..."

"Yes, I know they've helped too, but we see you around here. No one knows where they are or what they are doing. They blow in to Eternia, and blow back out again. You are more accessible and visible, thus you become the legend." Kali started pacing back and forth across the hallway, not noticnig the people starting to trickle in. "Kali, unless you want to talk to a lot of people, we really need to go," Rainy said when she noticed the others gathering. Kali stumbled to a halt and fear flickered briefly on her face before she drew herself up. Rainy grabbed her hand and dragged her down a stairwell. "We're in luck, a train is just arriving." They hurried on as soon as the doors opened. Within moments the train was in motion again. "This will take us to city center where there's a station, the busiest one in the city. It shouldn't take long to get a train back to Death City."

"Maybe I shouldn't have run..."

"Did you want to talk to them?"

"I don't know, but maybe I could have stopped this legend crap. Now they have even more to feed on." Kali slumped back in her seat and stared out at the tunnel slipping by.

"People need larger than life figures. It's something to aspire to."

"Aspire to? What a laugh. I'm nothing to aspire to. What does it take to make them realize that?"

"This isn't about your wants, it's about their needs."

"And what about my clay feet? What happens to their needs then?"

"I don't mean to be cold about this, but did anyone ever worry about you when you discovered the clay feet of one of your heroes? The same applies. That is for them to deal with."

"It just seems so weird," Kali commented as she returned to staring out the window.

"You were one of the invisible people in the Realms, weren't you? Best you can do is try and roll with it and be who you are to the best of your abilities. Let the others deal with their own issues. You'll go crazy otherwise. Now, you never did answer my question on your tattoo."

"Tattoo? Oh, right, I sort of designed it. I found the black work with the labrys and triangle on a temporary tattoo and had the artist help me add the snow leopard to the top." Kali turned back from the window to answer. "I'm sort of toying with the thought of getting either a piercing or another tattoo. Do you have anyone you'd recommend, or know anyone that could recommend a good artist or studio?"

"I haven't had any done myself, but most everyone at the Dans Macabre speaks highly of Death's Head Tattoo. It's just upstairs from Dans and in the main floor of where I live. What were you thinking of getting done?"

"Not sure yet. Still considering, but I've wanted more tats and a piercing or two for a while. Dans Macabre?"

"Our local version of the Devil's Cathouse. It's a goth club in Death City."

"I've heard of the Cathouse."

"You should check Dans out some time." The subway slowed to a stop at a brightly lit platform. "Well, this is the tube station for City Central Station. Upstairs they can get you on a train back to Death City." Kali stood and headed for the open doors. At the last minute Rainy joined her, "I can always catch another train back."

"I can find my way back..."

"I know that. I'm just enjoying talking to you and I'm not ready to end that." They walked up the wide flight of stairs and into a cavernous hall. Their footsteps echoed in the allmost empty expanse.

"I would have expected crowds."

"The city is huge but there aren't that many of us living in it right now. None of us knows why there is so much empty space, but it is weirdly enjoyable. You have some time to stay? I can show you some of the interesting parts."

"Uh, I don't know. Adaptation reaction won't let me stay still for long and it's starting to build up again."

"I could take you to Dans and you could burn off some energy dancing, if that's something you do."

"Yes, it's something I do." Kali followed Rainy as she headed for the main doors of the building. Outside she turned right down a wide cobbled street. They walked several long blocks between tall buildings, at first Kali expected something like New York but the architecture was weirder, more carvings, odd angles, and strange lines. Rainy turned left, crossed the street and started down another one. Five blocks ahead sunlight filtered in from a large clearing to the left. "Up ahead is the inner city park. It's about a kilometer wide and three kilometers long." A block before she turned right and pointed, "I live behind the cathedral, in that shorter brick building. Dans is in the basement, off an alley that runs from the cathedral back lot to the far street. Death's Head Tattoo is on the main floor of my building, next to a small deli." She walked slowly along an overgrown path past the cathedral, giving Kali plenty of time to take in the massive stone structure. "I have a killer view from my flat."

"No one maintains the cathedral?"

"I don't know, from the condition of the surroundings I'd guess not really. Religion has always creeped me out, so I haven't tried to go inside. You can, if you want."

"Maybe another day."

Rainy continued up the path around the back of the cathedral and to a narrow alley behind the centerline. She turned down the alley and walked about half way down it. Muted bass rythms drifted up a narrow stair, descending to a metal door. Red neon painted dancing letters in red flame on the wall above the stairs, spelling out, "Dans Macabre". Rainy opened the door and motioned Kali into the dark interior. Small clusters of people danced to the pounding music. A few more sat at the small tables around the edges or at the bar. "It fills up as night falls." Kali smiled and launched herself onto the floor.

An hour later she slipped into a chair by Rainy. "Thanks. This helped quite a bit. I should think about heading back soon. Was there anything else you wanted to show me this time?"

"The cathedral view, if you'd like." Kali nodded and Rainy led the way back out of the club. "Stairs or elevators?"

"Stairs, I can use the exercise."

Rainy cocked an eyebrow at Kali and returned to the area behind the cathedral. Along the wall of her building she started up a fire escape ladder. She climbed the steps to the last platform before the roof, ten floors up. She walked to the right end of the platform, where it ended in a windowed turret on the corner of the building. She opened the window facing the fire escape and climbed in. "There's inside stairs at the front of the building, near the elevators, but the view back here is so much better." Inside was a large, open room with a drafting table with drawings and notes scattered about and a second table with modeling clay, and tools.
