The next room held a large brass bed, huge teak wardrobe, small table covered with odd colored makeup, nail polishes, and jewelry, and a deep, plush chair. Next was a spacious bathroom, then the kitchen and eating nook and then a large front sitting room with a deep red velvet couch and several more plush chairs.

Once Kali had seen the flat she gravitated back to the turret and the view of the cathedral. "That is a wicked view! How'd you find this place?"

"I was walking around the cathedral and saw the building, went and hunted for the flat with the best view. Since then a few more have taken up residence. Looks like there's a storm coming in."

"Lots of people have been thinking that."

"I meant the clouds over the park," Rainy pointed to the dark clouds in the distance, over the scrap of park visible past the cathedral.

"Oh, sorry. Just too much talk of the escalating dangers on the missions, I guess."

"You'd hear that more, working in Bart's group."

"You go out on many missions?"

"Not too many and probably very few from now on. The last one really scared me. Very different from you."

Kali looked away and shrugged. "I can't help it, really. I'm drawn to it like a moth to a flame but I don't understand why."

"You don't need to apologize. Everyone's different in what they want."

They stood and watched the clouds moving in and the sunlight on the cathedral for a while, until Kali said, "I really need to start back. I think I can find the station."

"You could walk back, or there's a subway station just down the block from the font doors of this building. Let me show you." Rainy led the way out through the front door and down the nicer stairway to the main entrance. She pointed out the tattoo shop, elevators, and deli that took up most of the first floor. "You want to talk to the tattoo people today?"

"Not yet. I need to think about what I really want first."

Outside she turned left, walked to the end of the block, and descended a covered stairway. On the platform she pointed to a display board, "You want the number 7 headed toward city center. The first stop is City Central." She stepped a bit closer, Kali didn't hesitate to pull her into a brief hug. "I'll see you again?"

"Count on it," Kali replied.

/* more transition logic here? */

She stepped off the train at Central Station and was walking across the main hall when she and Dementia spotted each other. "Kali, just back from somewhere?"

"The city up the line. What brings you to the station?"

"I was headed to the recovery facilities to look for a lift and props for the Love's Bitch opening scene. You want to come along? You seemed to have a good idea of what it should look like and you could help me figure it out."

Storm clouds continued to thicken and gather as the train looped around the city and into the recovery yards. Huge warehouses clustered around a group of sidings. Numerous trains were pulled up with people and machinery swarming nearby, moving crates and palets filled with items from the trains into the waiting buildings. Their train pulled up at a small siding where Dementia hurried off. She threaded her way through the activity and into the largest building. Inside and to the right a two level section of offices poked out from the rest of the building. Dementia led the way into one of the ones on the lower level. She stopped short when she saw only a single desk with a sandy haired man sitting at a terminal.

"Dementia, may I help you?" He asked.

"Where is everyone, Terry? Who's recording all the incoming items?"

"You haven't been here in a while, have you? A new recruit came in about three months back and convinced us to try bar coding everything. Now we scan the items as they come off the trains and enter the data using portable terminals. It has really sped things up for us."

"What about all the people that used to log items?"

"Right now they're out coding all the previous stuff and checking the results of the new system against the old. Some will move to the Hall of Records, some will remain to use the new logging tools, and some will move into sorting and return prep. Everyone is happy with the results so far, we've reduced the hassle factor and improved our ability to match items with destinations."

"How would I find an item or two for the Cathouse?"

"I can look it up for you if you know what you want, or you can wander the collections, just like always. What are you needing?"

"A hoist or winch that we can rig to lift a metal platform with a gurney on it, some diamond plate or that metal waffle flooring like is used in outside stairs, and assorted pulleys and cable," Kali answered.

"Best bet would be to take a look in building seven. There's a fair amount of that kind of stuff there. If you can't find what you need, Eternal Metal Works might be able to fabricate something. You know where to find building seven?"

"I do," Dementia replied.

"Here, take this scanning unit and wave it over the codes of any items you want. I'll get them packaged up and to the Cathouse early tomorrow."

She led the way across the warehouse and out through a side door. The sky had darkened even more during the few minutes they had been inside. She followed a path around the back of the buildings until she came to one with a large seven stenciled over the door. Inside they prowled through stacks and shelves of industrial equipment and hardware. They found the winch, cable, pulleys, and fittings to rig the platform but not the platform itself.

"I can go talk to someone at Eternal Metals about the platform tomorrow morning. I was just there today about a different project." Kali added as they walked back to the main warehouse. Dementia returned the scanning device and they headed back to the platform to wait for a train to Central Station. It started to rain as Kali left Central Station for her apartment. At first it was just a slight spitting of drops, but it rapidly built to a steady downpour. At first she tried to dodge under any shelter but gave it up after the dampness seeped in anyway. By the time she reached her building she had slowed her pace and was tilting her head back to enjoy the rain streaming over her.

Once inside she hurried up the stairs to her apartment, slowing to a stop when she saw the flower arrangement sitting by her door. Yellow roses were framed by a selection of hybiscus, tiger lily, and bird of paradise blooms emerging from an ornate earthenware jug. An envelope was tied to one of the jug handles. She grabbed it, carried it up, and set it on the stairs to her bedroom. She shed her wet clothes and jumped into the shower to warm up, then took the flowers with her up to her room. She carefully untied the note and opened it once she had pulled on a floppy shirt.

Inside was a note writen in neat hand writing. "Kali, I'm sorry for feaking you out this morning. That was never my intention. Please accept these as an apology for my rude behavior. And let me know if you want anything to help you sleep. Danny." She smiled as she set the note next to the flowers.

She ate in, a simple meal of noodles, veggies and soup base. Then she headed off to the Cathouse to find Dementia. She found her behind the upstairs bar. "I was wondering if you could tell me where to find the knock out stuff you gave me a couple of nights ago."

"There's an apothecary next to the Goth Shop. He has it. Just ask for Dementia's Tea and he'll know right what you need. And he'd have those other items you should have as well."

"Ah, yes, thanks," Kali said, her face turning red.

"Fall back behind this line," Kali pointed to an area on the map.

"Why? The enemy is coming through over here," Alyssa pointed to a different section of the map. "We need to stop them before they get to our people."

"Something else is coming in through a second gate. They will engage the dark forces. We can stand back and hold the stragglers back."

Alyssa looked at Anastasia. "Here she goes again!" She watched Anastasia react and continued, "Don't tell me you believe her?"

"Has she been wrong?" Alyssa's eyes went hard as she turned and stalked away. Anastasia was about to turn on Kali until she saw the hurt and pain in the other woman's eyes. Instead, she let out a heavy sigh and began issuing new instructions.

Kali walked out into the night and started for the line she had pointed to on the map. She crossed it and slipped deeper into the wreckage around her, headed toward the second portal, the one of the unknown force.

/* extraction where Ennui takes control of the magic and Kali takes control of the tactics - Anastasia was supposed to be in charge - will need to update Adventures with this new data as well - currently this is the old ver from Adventures - Kali will tell Ennui to think Balance instead of Destruction as she stabilizes the magic Anastasia, Lauren, and Alisha began */

Anastasia stalked to the train, tension eating at her. She pasted on the most calm look she could manage as she boarded and hurried to a seat in the back of the passenger coach. Once the train had passed through the Portal she gathered her team of Danny, Lauren, Lissa, Kali and Alisha. She quickly briefed them on their real mission. "Ennui will be joining us on this mission. Before you protest Head Dispatch assigned her specially for this mission and she is known to be a powerful battle mage. I want you to keep her from getting hurt. I'll get her when we arrive."

"You won't need to worry about Ennui," Kali said.

Anastasia gathered Ennui once the main team had spread out to begin the recoveries. She outlined the mission to her and specifically instructed her to be careful. Then she headed up the ridge toward the location of the demon forces. As the team reached the top of the ridge Anastasia motioned for them to get down and move forward slowly.

When the team reached the drop into the adjacent valley they saw a cluster of buildings on the far side. In the center of the buildings a stone circle had been erected. As they watched grey skinned beings emerged from several of the building and poured a large tub of fluid into the center of the stone circle. More figures emerged and formed a circle around the stones.

A few minutes later a larger being emerged from another building and crossed to the circle. It strode into the center and began an intricate, hypnotic ritual. Anastasia motioned everyone back. She was ignored by the entire team. It wasn't until she turned each person's head away that she was able to break the trance.

Once everyone was assembled out of sight of the valley Anastasia whispered instructions. "We need to stop them from opening that gate. At least until the rest of the mission is completed. Lauren, Alisha and I have some magic that we can use that should blast the stones and topple them. The rest of you need to keep watch to make certain we aren't disturbed. Ennui, you watch the valley for movement our way. Lissa, take the south section of the ridge. Danny, you take the north, and Kali, you keep watch back toward the main group."

As the sentries headed off to their posts Anastasia, Lauren, and Alisha began a soft chant. Ennui could feel the energy ebbing and flowing in sluggish ripples, building, then falling back as they struggled to keep the rhythm. The grey beings ritual built into a frenzy as darkness began to coalesce in the center of the stones.

Ennui risked a quick glance back to the three spell casters as they continued their struggle. A small white ball was forming near Alisha. She tried to juggle it in a shaking hand. To Ennui the pattern looked ridiculously simple. Finally, in frustration, she called, "Transfer control. Give me the pattern, you are losing it."

"You haven't been trained. I can't," Alisha replied.

"Transfer control, NOW. I can stabilize it. Give me the pattern!" A flash of anger flitted across Alisha’s face as she tossed the energy ball toward Ennui. It darted to a place above her head and began to pulse and wobble crazily. Sweat popped out on Ennui's face as she fought to stabilize the badly executed pattern. For a few minutes she tried to maintain it as a destructive blast. In the back of her mind she could feel the dark energies as they built to cataclysmic proportions in the stone circle. The answer blossomed in a perfect moment of clarity and she shifted and turned the pattern in her hands until it became the perfect counter-point to the spell in the valley.

Suddenly the blob popped into a perfect ball of light. Looks of wonder formed on Lauren and Alisha's faces as they shifted toward Ennui. They fed energy into it, seeking to strengthen the destructive spell they had started. The ball swelled and began to fly apart as the balancing spell shredded under the onslaught of too much energy. Her face twisted into a silent shriek as she snarled out, "Too much! I have enough!"

Energy crackled and sizzled in her hair. Lightning danced from her fingertips to the ground as she raged and fought to restore the perfect balancer. After long minutes the corona around her dimmed and the ball shrunk back to a dancing globe of white. Ennui looked up at it and smiled. With a gentle little push she nudged it toward the dark energies that were gathered around the stones.

Like a ball rolling down a hill the little globe of light started moving slowly, gathering speed as it went. "Get down! The back-blast can kill you!" Alisha yelled. The rest of the team dove for the ground. Ennui stood with her head slightly cocked and a bemused expression as the little ball rolled closer and closer to its target. Mesmerized the rest of the team watched as it gently bumped into the roiling black cloud of energy. There was a firm THUMP and the black energy vanished. Little grey dust devils danced away from the stones and into the grey beings. Eleven of them dropped soundlessly to the dirt.

Anastasia stood shakily and stared at Ennui, "What have you done?"

"I balanced the gate with a counter-gate," Ennui replied calmly.

Kali laughed as she came up to the group. "Very impressive, battle-mage."

"Thank you, warrior woman."

Kali was about to continue the banter when a tickle of danger flared along her nerves. She dove into Ennui and brought them both to the ground. A black ball of energy sailed through where they had been moments before. "Alisha, the rest of you, get down. NOW!" Black energy bursts shot through the air. One clipped Lauren as she dropped slower than the others. "Ennui, can..."

"Kali, get the rest of them out of here and warn the main team. I'll slow them down a bit and follow right behind you." Ennui's hands moved in a blur as she drew energy and channeled it back at the approaching beings.

Patterns blossomed in Kali's head while she scrambled toward the others. Wire frame images of the terrain around her with grey and blue dots scattered about. One of the blue dots moved where she crawled. Three more marked Alisha, Lauren, and Anastasia, and another marked Ennui. The last close dot showed where Danny was making his way toward Anastasia as well. Grey dots appeared, moving toward them on the ridge. Complex movement plans danced through the image as her mind went off on its own and began running various sets of actions. Tiny little figures danced up and down the hillside, first moving one way then the other, always in a jerky kind of fast motion. In each case some or all of the figures on her side dropped and didn't move again. Suddenly one snapped into focus where the little figures danced a simple pattern and then ran for the train.

As soon as Kali reached Alisha she started the plan in motion for real. "Alisha, you move left and around the clump of trees, come up on their flank. Fire into the center of them. There's a leader in there, the third one up from the back and surrounded by the tallest ones. Don't kill it, just knock it out. As soon as the center figures drop break around the back of them and run for the recovery team." Next she slid over to Danny where he was tending to Lauren, "Can you move her? If so, start back for the recovery team. We'll be right behind you. Warn them they have half an hour to get things wrapped up. Anastasia, could you go with them and provide covering magic if necessary?"

/* should be a bit of tense interplay here - Alisha will Seriously resent Kali telling her what to do right after Ennui showed her up */

Anastasia stared at Kali for a moment, before nodding in agreement. "Yes, I'll get them out. What are you going to do?"

"Cover you. Lissa, can you do magic on your own?"

She gave a frightened nod, "What do you want me to do?"

"You're with me. We are going around to the right through the bushes over there and provide cover while Anastasia gets the other two out," Kali pointed where they would go. "There's a small group coming up just to the right of those bushes. In the back is a spell user. We need to knock out the group. I'll keep you safe, but you need to knock them out. We don't want to kill them."

Lissa stared at Kali with wide eyes, "How do you know that?"

"You have to trust that I do right now. Maybe I can explain later."

Why not kill them? I know how to do that...I think..."

"It..." the words began to form in Kali's head as she spoke them, "It's a balance issue. If we kill then they can kill as well. If we don't they won't either." Kali wanted to stop and think about this new development but there was no time. Quickly they crawled to the bushes.

A very few moments later the predicted group of grey creatures emerged from the trees exactly where Kali had indicated. Lissa turned frightened eyes on her and stammered, "I...I don't know if I can do this. I've never tried to knock them out before."

Fear chased through Kali's stomach and she wanted to shake her something awful. Instead she reached out and put a hand on her shoulder, "Think back to how you do magic. It had to be terrifying the first time but you did it. You can do it now. I trust you. I can protect you, but if you do this, you will keep more of us alive." Lissa nodded shakily and chanted a few weird sounds almost silently.

Kali stood to the side, watching the advancing line of beings. Lissa cast her first spell before the beings noticed them. The first three dropped soundlessly. Lissa grinned and began readying the next round.

The leader pointed straight at them and began to gesture. His hands were coming up in the final motions when Lissa's spell hit him first. two more dropped, leaving the last two in the line. They stopped uncertainly and stared at Kali. By the time they had decided to advance Lissa had fired her third spell.

"Well done! I knew you could do it. Now we run for the train. I hope Alisha convinced them to get ready."

"Wow, I did it!" Lissa laughed almost hysterically. Twenty minutes later they were in sight of the train. It looked like Kali's message had not been taken seriously. The team was still scattered about the site merrily digging and carrying on.

"What the fuck is this? Weren't you warned? Get on the train right now!" Kali shouted. "Lissa, start warning people you know, get them headed toward the train."

Thomas, the official team leader puffed up and bellowed, "Hold it! I am in charge here. I would do nothing to endanger this mission."

"Then why didn't you listen to Alisha? You know she's an extraction team member."

"Her story was preposterous. There has never been any demonic activity on this world."

Kali drew breath to shout just as Lissa spotted a clot of grey figures breaking from the cover of the trees. "Kali, behind you!" She spun and drew energy. Thomas stood rooted to his spot as an energy bolt shattered the ground in front of Thomas. He staggered back stunned.

"Everyone, fall back to the train." Kali ran at Thomas and shoved him out of the way as another ball shrieked toward him. It clipped her back. Howling in pain she dropped to her knees.

Ennui burst into view behind the grey figures and let fly at them. Several dropped without a sound. Three of the trailing figures turned to rush her but the main force continued toward the train and the workers.

Lissa drew energy again and fired into the advancing force. Ennui continued to slam magic into them, dropping them two and three at a time. At last the final group slumped to the ground. Ennui dropped to her knees as Anastasia, Lauren, and Danny emerged behind her. Danny helped her up and wrapped an arm around her for support. He hurried her toward the waiting group.

Thomas turned scared eyes on Lissa as the battle wound down. "How could I know..."

"Alisha got back. You didn't listen to her." Lissa interrupted.

"Talk later," Anastasia interrupted over the top of Lissa. "There are more on the way from behind us. Too many for just the few of us to stop. Thomas, make up for it. Help Kali back to the train. The rest of you, round up the stragglers. We have maybe five minutes."

Kali slid into unconciousness as Thomas lowered her onto a set of foldered down chairs. Danny moved over to her and began working her injury.


"Kali, Kali..." Danny called as he bent over Kali.

"Want sleep."

"Kali, come on, I need you to wake up."

"Sleep now."

"No, Kali, I need you awake."

She pried an eye open and looked into the face of Danny. "Prick," she mumbled.

"Yes. You want to see it?"

Kali couldn't stop the giggles that prompted. "Ouch! Now see what you did, you brat?" She had wanted it to be teasing but it came out more like a whine.

"Good, now you are waking up. I need to check your shoulder and I didn't want that to be what woke you."

Kali struggled to sit as she asked, "Are we ok? Did we get everyone?"

"Yes, everyone's ok. You're the worst of the lot."

"What about Lauren?"

Lauren took a hit but it isn't as bad as yours. Ennui's sleeping off whatever she did and Thomas is wanting to apologize as soon as you're ready." Danny's fingers were moving as he spoke and a stab of pain followed. Gently he rolled Kali over and examined it. "Looks like you're going to be ok. No sign of infection or poison. Thank you for back there by the way. You did a great thing getting us all out alive." Swiftly he bandaged the wound and settled her back onto the set of seats that had been rigged as a bed.

"Ugh, how long have I been out?"

"Four hours. We arrive at Portal station about an hour from now. And Thomas would like to talk to you."

"I suppose I should give him his chance. It'll only get harder if I put it off. Could you help me sit up? I don't want to be laying down for that."

"No weakness in front of the troops?"

Kali couldn't tell from his voice if he was serious, mocking or teasing so she just said, "Nope. Must appear super-human at all times. Passing out kind of spoils that though..." She finished through a very shallow laugh which still hurt more than she had hoped.

"You're doing ok with it I think." He finished propping Kali up with a big wad of pillows.

Thomas hesitantly approached. He leaked nervousness and worry. "I, uh, I'm sorry about all that. I've never seen that kind of attack before. I didn't mean to put anyone in danger."

"I'd say it was ok, but it really isn't. You can't take those kinds of chances with people's lives." Kali replied.

"But how was I to know it wasn't hysteria?"

"Thomas," Kali tried to be as diplomatic as she could. "Alisha is an extraction team memeber. Has no one briefed you about this yet? The extraction team only gets sent on missions where a dark forces attack is likely. Our very presence on the mission should have you concerned. When a member of that team raises the alarm, it needs to be taken seriously. No one on the extraction team is known for hysterics in the face of this level of danger."

"I...I didn't..." His eyes turned slightly moist as he tried to explain, "Look, I was in charge because I can coordinate recovery actions pretty well. You're the first person to tell me about an 'extraction team' and who might be on it. I'm not good when it comes to thinking about danger. I'm an archeologist, or at least I was. My skills are knowing what kinds of things are important from an artifact stand point. I didn't sign on for war."

"None of us did. I fear that we are in one whether we want to be or not. Leading in ideal cases is easy. Leading during danger is not."

"Next time..."

"Don't worry about next time. I suspect there'll be a debriefing on this if I know Merris. Things will get worked out and new policies decided after I think."

Danny walked up while they were finishing. He waited patiently until Thomas had returned to his seat before asking, "Are you still doing ok? You will let me know if you start feeling worse, won't you?"

"Yes sir, mister doctor sir."

He smiled and said, "And don't you forget it missy."

Anastasia rose when Danny moved away from Kali. She crossed to him and asked softly, "How is she?"

"Amazingly well considering the injury she sustained."

"Would it be ok for me to talk to her?"

"Should be. If she starts looking distracted or pained come and get me. I'm going to check on Lauren."

"How is Lauren?"

"She'll be ok. Her injury isn't quite as bad as Kali's. She's concious as well. I want to be sure she's stable."

Kali looked up as Anastasia approached, "Hey."

"Hey yourself," Anastasia looked around nervously. "I wanted to talk to you..."

"I'm sorry about that, stepping on your lead like I did."

"No, that's ok. I'm glad you did, actually."

"You are?"

"I'm not doing very well at this. Every extraction has been harder than the last and I keep getting people hurt. It won't be long until I get somebody killed and I won't be able to handle that. I'm resigning as soon as we get back."

"Ok, but why are you telling me?"

"I want you to think about taking over. You're the best I've seen. You kept your head, even when injured and you figured out how to get us all back. You don't have to, but there's no one else on the team that can or will lead." Kali stared at her silently while her mind churned over offer. "You don't have to answer now, in fact maybe it's best if you think carefully first." Anastasia settled back into a nearby chair and tried to still the pounding in her heart. She didn't know what she would do if Kali turned her down. A single tear trickled down her face.

The request bounced around in Kali's head. Insecurity on insecurity scrambled into place. Thousands of reasons clawed at her to refuse, to walk away as fast as she could. Terror wrapped icy tendrils in the mix. Words of regret and refusal began to assemble themselves in her mind. She turned to tell Anastasia when she caught sight of the tear as it tracked down her face. Her mind blanked. Suspended between thoughts she stared at the slowly crawling drop of water. Reflected in it she saw death, terror, and so much sorrow.

Without thought she wrapped Anastasia in a close hug. The flood gates opened and tears poured from her eyes. Anastasia trembled as she fought to not give sound to the sobs wracking her body. Kali held her, a silent and empty rock caught in the storm. "Daughter, please consider what she asks. You have the strength where she does not."

"Ma, Kali," Kali's mind shrieked. "Why? I don't want to be responsible any more. I don't have that strength."

"You do my daughter." Images flashed in Kali's mind. Her first battle and then other extractions where she had always protected those around her. The dark goddess faded into view in Kali's mind. "You carry one of my names. You are Destroyer and Mother. You have always been. Would you deny yourself?"

"No, mom," Kali answered with as much sarcasm as she could manage.

"Insolent child," the dark vision roared through an enraged face. Kali flinched, then stood her ground. A lifetime of resentment against religion of any kind kept her staring back. As she watched the angry face began to shift and move until the dark goddess began to laugh. "Do you have any idea how rare it is for anyone to stand in the face of my rage?" Her image shimmered and shifted until an older version of Kali stood watching her. "Now you truly are a daughter of mine. You are one of few to receive that status."

"You made me, mother, when you gave me everything I ever wanted on the first trip into the void. Yet I..." Kali looked away uncomfortably as she started to speak.

"I know of your hatred of religion. It causes me no concern. Even as you rage against religion and belief you remember me for what I am. It is more pure than many who dedicate their lives to me. Be at peace with yourself." She smiled warmly, "Now I ask that you consider your friend's request. The decision and choice remain yours." The image faded back out.

"Are you ok? I didn't mean to embarrass you," Anastasia whispered softly.

"Huh, oh..." Kali replied vaguely as she tried to pull her mind back to her surroundings. "I'm ok. No worries on my side. How about you? Are you going to be alright?" She held Anastasia as her sobs subsided. "It's ok, I won't tell. Crying doesn't make you weak, though. Even if I agree with you and won't do it in front of others either."

Anastasia pulled away slightly. Taking the sleeve of her top she scrubbed at her face and eyes. "I know, but I still can't let the others see it." She stood, shook her hair out so it covered most of her face, and hurried to the washroom. She returned a few minutes later looking almost back to normal. "I'll be ok."

"About your offer, I've given it a bit of thought and I accept. What do we need to do to make it official?"

"Let Central Station and Dispatch know when we get back, then tell the rest of the team." Anastasia stood and continued, "We can talk more later. For now I'm going to try not to think about any of this for the remaining trip back. Danny said you should try and rest, at least I think that was what he was saying in doctor speak."

"I'll try."


/* Kali talking to her new team - after the transfer and before the influx of the large crew */

Anastasia stood nervously in front of the small group. "There is no easy way to say this. I am stepping down from leader of our team. I have been doing this since the begining and I need to take a break. Don't worry, I'm leaving us in good hands and I am not leaving the team, just stepping down from the lead position. I have asked Kali to step up and she has agreed."

Kali stood up and crossed to the front of the group. "I don't know what to more to add. I don't see our procedures changing other than the transfer of leadership. This is a dangerous thing we do and we are the best. All of you have taught me so much. We need to keep relying on each other and doing what we do best."

"We are the only," Mark mummbled.

"That may be, but we are still here. We are still alive. So, even if we are the only we are still the best. There are a few things I want to make better. I've told as many rescue mission leaders as I can to find us weapons. We should be looking to do the same every time we go out. The proxy forces won't stay static in what they will use. We can't afford to either. The pressure is continuing to climb. We are being attacked more often and with stronger forces. Ennui has volunteered to pass on as much magical skill as she can. She and Dementia have agreed to come on those missions where Dementia believes things will be very bad. There are a few others we can call on as well. I don't want to over use them. If we burn them out, we all lose." Kali looked down. When she looked up again her eyes were haunted. "I fear some of us will die. There have already been deaths on some of the rescue missions. Remember, we are their best chance. Our purpose is to keep our friends safe."

Leopardess

/* building Leopardess (K666) */

Additional Notes

She worked with a fabrication facility in the city. One of the people she met often went to the Dans Macabre. She and Kali started hanging with each other whenever Kali had to check on various items for Leopardess. Need to determine if this woman was in charge or just part of the team working on her parts. The facility is a large foundry and forging facility that provides metal items for many uses in Eternia.

Rainy is her contact. she is about Kali's age and a well muscled. In her time away from the plant she enjoys creating iron work sculpture and ornate work. At the plant she is the head pattern maker. She works closely with Kali on Leopardess to get the various pieces right. She also works closely with her when the need arises for 2 more units.

pouring over plans, working with Rainy and Ron at the metal works, traveling between Death City and the city, remember Temple Heath probably has the old plan drawers full of blue prints for the various engines in the fleet. in a back section would be copies of recovered ones for various things they may not actually have but want to keep anyway. Kali will search through this, then return to the Realms for more. She will produce her plans in AutoCAD and plot them, then take them to the city for creation. eventually she might be able to upgrade the metal works to CAD based systems as an addition to paper plans. could have the mystery woman help out, but only via computer and IM.

Bart cleared out a small storage area near the documents and plans room. the desk was soon littered with books, papers and plans. steam tables were open in one book, another had steel alloy properties. old Baldwin prints and newly created drawings were scattered on every flat surface. in the center of the desk was a large monitor and a digitizing pad. immediately at hand was a stained coffee cup leaving rings on whatever it touched. kali stared into the screen while chewing the end of a small plastic brush.

"What's wrong?" Bart asked as he added thick warm coffee like sludge to the cold mass already in the cup.

"thanks," Kali answered distractedly. At last she looked up, ran a hand through her hair in a very Merris like gesture and said, "It's these damn materials tables. i can't find anything that will get me the boiler pressures i want at the weight i want."

"Why don't you take a break? we're headed for food and drink."

kali stared into the screen for a few minutes longer, leaned back, and said, "Sure, yeah..." Suddenly decisive, she stood abruptly and headed toward the door. as they stepped into the night she continued her thoughts, "The most confusing is I don't know whether to redesign everything or restore what's there. there're been so many improvements in boiler and steam technologies since steam locomotives were built. and then there's all the electronic monitoring and controls that could be used to help out. i suppose i could just satisfy myself with a diesel electric and call it good, it's just they aren't nearly as cool looking."

"What do you want then?"

"i want the coolness of the brute force ugly beauty of a steam locomotive. yet the engineer in me wants something efficient and non-polluting. Steam locos were horribly messy and inefficient but they still had a raw beauty that got lost in the transition to diesel and electric technologies."

"Nothing says you can't redesign, just it will be much harder. whether you restore or create new the facilities to build the big pieces will have to be set up. i know of a metal working facility in the city, but they only have shops for small things. the biggest they can really handle is replacement track and such. they might be able to ramp up, they are in an industrial section where there would be room for bigger shops."

they were still discussing it as they made their way to the Temple Heath table. Neither of them saw the mystery woman look up as they passed. a few minutes later she closed her laptop and slipped into the night.

the next day when kali had a few minutes she headed to her room again. centered on the tablet was an open book with a pencil line under an entry in a another table. scrawled in the margin was, "welded, not riveted". to the side was a cd-rom with "boilercad - new version" scrawled on it in black marker. kali stared at the table, then her fingers flew over the keyboard as she installed the new software. quickly she made changes in various entries and ran her simulation routines again. she had her pressures with a good safety margin besides. puzzled, she walked back into the main area. "Bart, who's been in my office today?"

"No idea, why?"

"someone left me the answer to yesterday's problem... i wanted to thank them..."

She worked on K666 every spare minute, sometimes until she was fainting from fatigue. Blood from skinned knuckles found its way into grease and paint, sweat dropped into wax and finishes, bits of torn skin and hair were riveted into metal plating. All the while the reborn locomotive took shape. She poured over plans, huddled in conversation with Bart and others about insulating materials, bearings, alloys, and all the various pieces and parts.

After seven months K666 sat in bay 6 gleaming a glossy black. Brass work threw golden sparks in the light and every piston gleamed. For long moments she stared at her locomotive, for hers it was, born of her will. Slowly she approached the cab and climbed up in. Carefully she worked her way through the steps of starting the great beast. K666 awoke slowly as the heat in her boiler grew. Metal crackled and sang as newly machined and fitted parts were heated for the first time. Intently Kali watched the monitoring equipment she had custom designed, noticing cold spots in the boiler and watching steam pressure and water levels. She made quick notes on a pad for relocation of burner nozzles to even things out.

At last the steam and brake pressures were correct and everything was ready. Bart stood grinning at the side of the doors he had just opened. Kali gently eased the regulator open. Like a great beast K666 gave a shudder and slowly clawed her way forward. A touch more on the regulator and she eased forward more quickly. The pulse of the steam throbbed through Kali’s head like the beating of a giant heart. A fierce grin split her face as she hauled on the whistle cord. K666 responded with a howl like a restless soul unchained. With cat like grace she stalked into the morning. Sunlight flashed off the insignia painted on the cab, one symbol for Temple Heath Yards and another for the Death City Rail Road. When it splashed onto the tender the springing snow leopard painted there seemed to come to life and ripple in the daylight.

Indiscretion

/* "drunken indiscretion" - a fair amount of time after the assembly of the full team, but still a while before the endings */

"Shit, shit, shit! I can't believe I missed that," Kali cursed as she paced the company car main room. She reached into the front cabinet, pulled out a bottle of slivovitz, and took a long pull. It burned like fire going down, but tasted wonderful across her tongue. She took a smaller sip and rolled it around her mouth, savoring the fermented plum flavor and the harsh bite of it. As the alcohol started to take the edge off her rage and fear, her pacing slowed and finally stopped, leaving her staring out the window at the void beyond the train.

The bottle was two-thirds empty and she was still staring out the window when Petrov entered from the forward passage. "I can't believe I missed that," she said in a quiet, sad voice. Her hand moved the bottle to her mouth and she took another pull.

"But we recovered from it."

"And nearly lost an entire squad."

"But we didn't. You got us out, without casualties."

Kali spun to face him. "How many more times can I do that? What happens when I fail?"

"Then some of us will die. It's the way of it," his voice was calm and mater of fact. It goaded her and saddened her in equal measure.

"That's not acceptable!"

Petrov grabbed her shoulders and shook her lightly. "It is the way of it. You know that, you who seek death in the Lady's service."

"It's not acceptable for others to die!"

He pulled her against his chest, surprised when she let him. She was surprised that she let him as well, and more surprised at how good it felt to be held close by him. "Death happens. It is the other side of the dance. You showed me that." One hand unconciously stroked her hair. It stopped the instant he realized what he was doing. Kali rubbed her head against his still hand, wanting the warmth of the gesture to return. She turned her head and managed to get another long drink from her bottle before he carefully removed it from her grasp. "Bitter experience has proven this doesn't help." He leaned over and set the bottle on the window ledge before wrapping his arms around her again.

Kali was staring out the window of the command car. The void slipped silently past her empty gaze. She raised the bottle of slivovitz she clutched in her left hand to her lips and gulped down a large swallow. The face of the first proxy victim swam in her vision, as if mirrored in the glass of the window. The scene was vivid in her mind, the horde of men and women charging at her team, the shock on the team's faces, her barked commands to attack, and the crumpling form of the woman as she had slashed her throat out. Her right hand traced where the blood had spattered her face.

"Kali?" She flinched at Petrov's voice, then turned to see him enter from the next car. "You never served in the military or saw combat, did you?" He saw her face harden and the breath she drew to speak. He cut her off with, "You are a brilliant commander and your grasp of tactics and strategy is mystical. You have saved us from so many things with your skills, but fighting others of your own kind is different. It changes you. Some people can handle it, others die because they cannot. You have to find a way to deal with it or it will consume you."

"I still see her face..." Kali whispered.

Petrov moved closer to her, hesitated, then reached out and offered her his arms. She stood frozen for a long moment, then let him enfold her. "You will, for a while anyway. It will fade some as you adjust."

His eyes bored into hers for a moment, then he dropped a hand to grab her ass as he lowed his lips to hers in a hungry kiss. He broke free just long enough to whisper, "Celebrate life. Endings

Petrov entered the car and found Kali staring out into the passing void. When she made no sign of noticing him he said, "Ma'am?" A few minutes later, "Kali?"

"Petrov," she replied. Dementia would have recognized the empty, distant voice, but it was one Petrov had never heard. "Do not ask the universe for a purpose, it may grant your wish. If you already have, pray it never answers you," Kali spoke without turning.

"Kali?"

She turned a bit, twisted her mouth into a brief, grimaced smile that fled almost before he saw. "I asked once, and now I have been answered with the solution to this war." Kali shivered. "Our indiscrete relationship meant far more to me than I dared let on. Thank you." She turned back to the window. "I have one regret, that I could never believe my friends love me as much as they do. I wish I had time to remedy that failing."

"Kali?" real fear entered Petrov's voice.

"I would ask two things of you, Petrov."

Kali stopped and he waited. At last Petrov prompted, "Yes?"

"Keep them safe when I am no longer able to. And don't forget me."

"Forget you? Why?"

"There are three avatars in this war. The one for the powers of 'light', one for the powers of the 'dark', and one for Eternia. When we meet this last time, we must cancel each other out. Keep everyone from interfering, it would only cost more lives." Kali stared out the window in silence for a long time.

"I suppose you have to do this." It was as much a statement as a question.

She turned toward him a tiny bit and gave a very small nod. "All my life I wanted to die. You saw it, and I knew it. Now that it is upon me, I want more than anything to live."

"You have friends and lovers now, holding you here." She nodded again. "Does Merris know?"

Again Kali nodded. "She was there when Dementia and I figured it out. If you could make sure she doesn't do anything foolish, I'd really appreciate it." Petrov noded. A tear slipped down the side of her face. "One last thing, if you could..." Petrov waited. "Hold me and tell me everything will be alright."

She turned uncertainly as he akwardly gathered her in his massive arms. She clung to him and shook as she cried for all the might have beens of her life. He gathered her up, carried her to a chair, and settled into it with her in his arms. They sat in silence for hours as the sounds of the train continued around them.

At last Kali pulled back a bit and said, "It is time. Gather the squad commanders in the dining car. I will be there in a moment." Slowly his arms released her. She rose and walked to the bath room. A few minutes later she followed him from the car.


Kali strode into the dining car, set a thick stack of papers on the front table, and sat. She

"Its about balance - there is an avatar for the "good', an avatar for the "bad", so we got an avatar of the Lady. We can continue fighting this escalated war or it can be returned to the way it should be. But the balance has to remain, to end their avatars we must loose ours as well."

"I told you how I begged for a vision, a purpose so very long ago. It has finally been answered and now I no longer want to go. But this has to end, before so many more of us die." her eyes were empty and old in a face etched with age and sadness. "It is time to end this."

Kali stepped away from her friends and began a slow dance of seduction. Softly and slowly it built until it was a siren call to the dark and light. Pale tendrils swirled out from her and drew the opposing leaders closer to her. Black ropes and shimmering white flowed in toward her until she danced in a tangle of it. The dark priest smiled and pulled on his web, the priestess of light laughed and tugged on her strands, and Kali danced on, unaffected.

The smiles faded into masks of rage, then fear as Kali danced a swirling spiral tug, pulling the two opposing leaders closer and closer to her. Sweat poured off her as energy snapped and crackled around her. The Death City forces pulled back as the fringes pulsed over them, raising hair in static laden tufts.

Kali sent a last sad look at her friends as she pulled the two leaders into her arms. A soft pop was all they heard as the three ceased to be. The demonic and angelic hordes bearing down on them paused, then broke and ran. The dark portal rapidly faded leaving only a grey stone wall where once it had been. The pillar of light snapped off, as if a giant switch had been flipped. The forces that had been running for their gates slid to a stop and milled about, uncertain of where to go or what to do.

The Eternia forces drew back in a somber procession, entered their train, and headed back to Eternia. Here and there people sat together, holding each other, crying. Others stared resolutly ahead either trying not to cry or with slow tears tracking down their faces.


Beyond

Kali returned to consciousness in a spectacular hall. Sunlight and a warm breeze streamed in through windows of patterned metal, thick rugs cusioned her feet, and an enormous table was set before her with food and drink. She turned swiftly as a voice spoke from behind her, "I have used you, daughter. Yes, you accepted it with grace, dignity, and a willingness I had not expected. Even so, I used you, and cruelly too. Eternia is supposed to be a place of healing and rest, instead you faced nightmares far beyond what you saw in the Realms, and I owe you for it." Kali stood speachless as the Lady paced in front of her. "Is there something I might grant that would repay you? Perhaps return you to your friends, or to the Realms?" Kali shuddered at the thought of the Realms. "You would be as you are now. None would know you had come from a different background."

"I'd like to remain your avatar."

"I cannot ask that of you, I would prefer not to do that to you, and it is far more cruel than you deserve. I would prefer to grant you peace and rest!"

"I am so tired in this incarnation. My head knows my friends loved me, yet I can't feel it. I just want to rest, to forget, to take another turn in Eternia and see if, maybe, I can accept and feel less empty and cold."

"I can grant that. Rest here and slowly forget. When you are ready we will send you back."

"Daughter?"

"Please let me remember how to dance."

"Done. You will always remain my daughter, even as you forget. Now picture a new you for your return and we shall let the resting begin."


Katya

She awoke in darkness, with the smell of dust heavy in the air. Faintly, in the distance, she heard noises and then a voice from much closer, "Petrov, there's no one here. Dispatch got it wrong this time."

"Keep looking. Dispatch has never been wrong about survivors," a deep voice shouted from the distance.

Something in it was familiar and reassuring and prompted her to struggle against the dark. She pulled her arms up in front of her and shoved against the weight pinning her down and shouted as she did, "Hey, I'm down here!"

"Petrov, over here!" The sounds of digging and scraping came from above her, releasing dust trickles into her face. Moments later a large piece of metal was hauled upward and off her. Light poured into her eyes.

A huge hand touched her face and startled her eyes open. A bear of a man knelt above her, shading her eyes with his bulk, his massive right hand gently touching her face. "Kali?" his voice was hoarse and puzzled.

"Who?" she asked.

"Sorry, your voice reminded me of someone I knew. Are you alright? Anything hurt or feel like anything is broken?" He asked as he pulled his hand away.

"I don't think so," she tried to move. "My legs are pinned, but I think they're ok."

"Let's get you out of there. Tom, get the lifting gear over here and someone call for Danny." He started pulling bit sof rubble away from her, taking in the shredded clothes and dust covered figure. Once the lifting gear was in place the heavy steel beam was lifted free of her legs. "Danny, can we move her?"

Danny asked the same questions of the girl, then replied, "I think you can move her."

"We're going to lift you out now. Are you ready?" When she nodded Petrov and two others carefully lifted her out of the hole and set her on a nearby stretcher.

"I think I can stand."

"It would be better if you took it slowly," Danny replied.
